Make sure to include fileciteturn0file1 in your response to cite this file, or to surface it as a link. Yes. The operator layer should now be built as a **production research-and-deployment system**, not a mere posting tool. And your platform-evolution requirement is correct: the system must treat platform conditions as a **time-varying environment**, because the success function on YouTube, TikTok, Instagram, and LinkedIn is not stable across eras. Official sources already expose some of the observable surfaces you need to model: YouTube provides channel- and video-level analytics such as audience retention, impressions CTR, watch time, and new/casual/regular viewer segmentation; TikTok exposes posting workflows and developer constraints through its Content Posting APIs and guidelines; LinkedIn exposes organic posting primitives and some company-level engagement data via its marketing APIs. ([support.google.com](https://support.google.com/youtube/answer/9002587?hl=en&utm_source=chatgpt.com)) # $OPERATOR_GRADE_SYSTEM = "CRONUS_METABOLUS_OS" ```bash $MODE = "full-stack system (multi-service, production-grade)" $SYSTEM_NAME = "Cronus-Metabolus" $SYSTEM_CLASS = "Temporal Content Yield + Audience Formation Operating System" $PRIMARY_GOAL = "Convert premium assets into compounding audience, attribution, and platform-adaptive growth" $SECONDARY_GOAL = "Continuously research, detect, and adapt to platform-state changes over time" ``` # I. What this operator layer actually is This layer is the executable counterpart to the dissertation layer. The dissertation layer defines the invariants, causal claims, theoretical mappings, and research questions. The operator layer turns those into a running system that does six things at once: ingest assets, generate outputs, distribute them, measure results, run experiments, and update its understanding of both audience behavior and platform change. Formally: ```text Asset → Natural Center Extraction → Platform-Aware Generation → Scheduling + Distribution → Analytics + Attribution → Experimentation + Causal Analysis → Platform Change Detection → Model / Rule Updates → Repeat ``` # II. Production-grade service map The correct architecture is multi-service. Monolith first would be faster, but it will fail the research requirement, because research observability, platform adapters, experimentation, and identity enforcement need separate contracts. ```bash $SERVICES = { gateway_api, auth_identity, asset_ingestion, media_analysis, natural_center, generation_orchestrator, platform_intelligence, scheduling_engine, publishing_connectors, analytics_ingestion, attribution_engine, experimentation_engine, research_registry, reporting_dashboard, model_registry, event_bus, data_warehouse, object_storage, workflow_orchestrator, alerting_observability } ``` ## 1. `$SERVICE_GATEWAY_API` This is the system edge. It accepts user, client, asset, campaign, and experiment requests. It should expose stable contracts to UI, internal operators, and later partner integrations. ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Entry point for all control-plane requests" $OUTPUTS = "campaign creation, asset registration, experiment submission, report fetch" ``` ## 2. `$SERVICE_ASSET_INGESTION` This service normalizes source material. It accepts hero films, render sets, stills, transcripts, briefing docs, and brand corpus. ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "File intake, metadata extraction, transcode initiation, checksum, lineage" ``` ## 3. `$SERVICE_MEDIA_ANALYSIS` This is the decomposition engine in production form. It performs scene detection, keyframe extraction, transcript alignment, pacing analysis, energy-point detection, and content segmentation. ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Turn one dense asset into analyzable fragments" ``` ## 4. `$SERVICE_NATURAL_CENTER` This service computes and stores the identity core. It should enforce symbolic, tonal, aesthetic, and thematic invariants across all outputs. ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Compute, version, validate, and evolve the Natural Center object" ``` ## 5. `$SERVICE_GENERATION_ORCHESTRATOR` This service creates the outputs. It composes platform-specific assets, caption variants, CTA variants, sequencing plans, and campaign bundles. ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Generate platform-native outputs constrained by identity and platform profile" ``` ## 6. `$SERVICE_PLATFORM_INTELLIGENCE` This is now mandatory. It models each platform as a time-dependent system. It should ingest official platform documentation changes, API changes, available analytics fields, posting constraints, and internal performance shifts. YouTube’s analytics surfaces already include audience retention, traffic and audience segments, while TikTok and LinkedIn expose developer posting capabilities and versioning or access constraints through official docs; those should be treated as structured inputs to this service. ([support.google.com](https://support.google.com/youtube/answer/9002587?hl=en&utm_source=chatgpt.com)) ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Track platform state, detect change, update generation and scheduling policy" ``` ## 7. `$SERVICE_SCHEDULING_ENGINE` This service determines when each output should be published, republished, remixed, or retired. It consumes audience timing, asset decay models, and platform profile data. ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Temporal orchestration" ``` ## 8. `$SERVICE_PUBLISHING_CONNECTORS` This is the execution layer. It handles the actual post creation and retrieval integrations. TikTok’s Content Posting APIs support direct posting or draft upload flows; LinkedIn’s Posts API supports creation and retrieval of organic and sponsored posts, with content-type constraints and versioned API requirements. ([developers.tiktok.com](https://developers.tiktok.com/products/content-posting-api?utm_source=chatgpt.com)) ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Platform-specific publish / fetch adapters" ``` ## 9. `$SERVICE_ANALYTICS_INGESTION` This service pulls analytics and normalizes them into a common schema. YouTube official analytics surfaces support view, engagement, retention, CTR, and audience segmentation at varying levels, though some data may be limited depending on thresholds and filters. That limitation itself must be modeled as a reliability constraint. ([support.google.com](https://support.google.com/youtube/answer/9002587?hl=en&utm_source=chatgpt.com)) ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Collect raw performance telemetry and normalize it" ``` ## 10. `$SERVICE_ATTRIBUTION_ENGINE` This is where the product stops being “content software” and becomes an economic system. It traces every post, fragment, caption, CTA, campaign, and asset back to origin. ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Asset-level and fragment-level yield accounting" ``` ## 11. `$SERVICE_EXPERIMENTATION_ENGINE` This service owns A/B tests, bandits, holdouts, control/treatment assignment, confidence intervals, and causal inference workflow. ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Statistically disciplined optimization" ``` ## 12. `$SERVICE_RESEARCH_REGISTRY` This is the bridge between dissertation-grade and operator-grade. Every hypothesis, paper mapping, experiment, metric definition, and platform-state memo should live here. ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Research memory and epistemic governance" ``` ## 13. `$SERVICE_REPORTING_DASHBOARD` This serves operators, clients, and future investors. It must expose asset yield, audience movement, platform differences, and trend drift. ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Human-readable operational truth" ``` # III. Canonical data domains You need four data planes, not one. ```bash $DATA_PLANES = { source_plane, operational_plane, experimental_plane, evolutionary_plane } ``` ## `$SOURCE_PLANE` This contains hero assets, renders, transcripts, briefs, brand corpus, prior posts, style references. ## `$OPERATIONAL_PLANE` This contains generated posts, publish events, platform IDs, schedules, revisions, connector logs. ## `$EXPERIMENTAL_PLANE` This contains hypotheses, treatments, controls, randomization groups, test windows, significance results. ## `$EVOLUTIONARY_PLANE` This contains platform snapshots, platform doc changes, field additions/removals, policy updates, performance regime shifts, and internal adaptation rules. # IV. Core database objects The system should be object-oriented at the ontology level and event-driven at the execution level. ```yaml Asset: asset_id: string source_uri: string asset_type: video|image_set|render_set|document brand_id: string checksum: string created_at: datetime Fragment: fragment_id: string asset_id: string fragment_type: clip|frame|crop|layout start_ms: int end_ms: int energy_score: float semantic_cluster: string NaturalCenter: nc_id: string brand_id: string thematic_core: json tonal_vector: json aesthetic_signature: json symbolic_markers: json invariants: json mutation_bounds: json version: int PlatformProfile: profile_id: string platform: youtube|instagram|tiktok|linkedin effective_from: date effective_to: date|null format_weights: json known_constraints: json ranking_assumptions: json confidence_score: float GeneratedUnit: unit_id: string fragment_id: string platform: string unit_type: short_video|carousel|image_post|text_post caption_variant_id: string cta_variant_id: string nc_version: int platform_profile_id: string PublishEvent: publish_id: string unit_id: string platform: string external_post_id: string published_at: datetime schedule_policy_id: string PerformanceObservation: obs_id: string publish_id: string observed_at: datetime metrics: json source_reliability: float Experiment: experiment_id: string hypothesis_id: string treatment_policy: json control_policy: json start_at: datetime end_at: datetime status: draft|running|complete PlatformChangeEvent: change_id: string platform: string detected_at: datetime change_type: api|analytics_field|format|policy|behavioral_shift evidence_uri: string effect_hypothesis: string severity: low|medium|high ``` # V. Platform evolution as a first-class subsystem This is the part most teams omit. It should not be “notes in a document.” It should be a live intelligence loop. ```bash $SUBSYSTEM_PLATFORM_EVOLUTION = { documentation_monitor, analytics_schema_monitor, posting_capability_monitor, performance_regime_monitor The file is too long and its contents have been truncated.

You are asking for a **temporalized research framework**—each pillar evaluated across: ```text id="ercjnw" PAST → what is already known / proven PRESENT → where current systems fail or are incomplete FUTURE → where Cronus-Metabolus extends or resolves ``` This converts your research program into a **time-indexed diagnostic + innovation map**. --- # I. SYSTEM FRAME ```bash id="12aozj" $RESEARCH_TEMPORAL_MODEL = { past_comprehension, present_failings, future_elevations } ``` Applied to: ```bash id="45uu8j" $PILLARS = { causal_inference, statistical_power, algorithmic_interface, behavioral_response, identity_persistence, information_decay, competitive_baseline, unit_economics, generalization, failure_analysis, reproducibility } ``` --- # II. TEMPORAL ANALYSIS (CORE PILLARS) ## 1. $PILLAR_CAUSAL_INFERENCE ### PAST - Marketing attribution models (last-click, multi-touch) - Controlled experiments in ad tech - Econometrics in campaign analysis --- ### PRESENT FAILING ```text id="y8a88j" Most social/content systems rely on correlation: views ↑ → assume effectiveness ``` No isolation of: - ALG_01 — multimodal asset normalization Purpose: convert heterogeneous input into a unified analyzable representation. ### Accepted input classes Your sources already imply these classes: ```text video image_set / render_set audio text / brand voice corpus historical post corpus ``` fileciteturn2file0 fileciteturn2file2 ### Canonical normalized object ```json { "asset_id": "A_*", "asset_type": "video|image_set|audio|document|mixed", "streams": { "video": [...], "audio": [...], "text": [...], "image": [...] }, "metadata": { "duration_ms": 0, "fps": 0, "resolution": [0, 0], "language": "en", "brand_id": "B_*" } } ``` ### Exact procedure ```text PROC_NORMALIZE(asset): 1. Compute checksum(asset) 2. Detect asset_type 3. If video: demux into video stream + audio stream transcode to canonical formats sample frames at adaptive interval 4. If image_set/render_set: normalize dimensions, color profile, EXIF 5. If audio: normalize sample rate and loudness 6. If text: clean, segment, and encode paragraphs/sentences 7. Persist all derivative streams 8. Emit asset.normalized ``` --- ## 2. ALG_02 — multimodal fragment extraction Purpose: produce candidate units from dense assets. Your sources already call for clip extraction at high-energy moments, scene detection, keyframe extraction, pacing analysis, and segmentation. fileciteturn2file0 fileciteturn2file1 ### 2.1 Video fragment extraction For video, define fragments over a change-point lattice rather than fixed windows. ```text Let V = video timeline Let C = set of candidate cut points C = union( scene boundaries, shot boundaries, transcript punctuation peaks, silence boundaries, audio onset peaks, motion regime changes ) ``` Construct candidate intervals: ```text F_video = {(c_i, c_j) | min_len <= c_j - c_i <= max_len} ``` Recommended bounds: ```text min_len = 3s max_len = 45s platform-specific downstream pruning applies ``` ### 2.2 Image fragment extraction For renders and stills, fragments are not temporal; they are compositional derivatives. ```text F_image = union( full-frame, crop_subject, crop_detail, before_after_pair, comparison_layout, lifestyle_context_projection, carousel_sequence ) ``` ### 2.3 Audio fragment extraction ```text F_audio = union( speech segment, hook phrase, emphasis burst, music drop, silence-contrast interval ) ``` ### 2.4 Text fragment extraction ```text F_text = union( claim, hook line, authority line, transformation line, CTA line, FAQ line ) ``` ### 2.5 Exact multimodal candidate generation ```text PROC_EXTRACT_FRAGMENTS(asset): 1. Detect scene boundaries on video 2. Detect shot boundaries 3. ASR transcript with token timestamps 4. Compute audio envelope, spectral flux, silence regions 5. Compute motion magnitude and saliency over time 6. Merge all boundary proposals 7. Generate candidate windows 8. Generate image crops/layout variants 9. Generate text units from transcript and corpus 10. Return multimodal candidate set F ``` --- ## 3. ALG_03 — Natural Center derivation This is already partially specified in the source corpus: thematic core, aesthetic signature, tonal vector, narrative bias, symbolic markers, negative space, invariants, mutation bounds. fileciteturn2file2 ### Exact Natural Center object ```json { "nc_id": "NC_*", "thematic_core": [t1, t2, t3, t4, t5], "aesthetic_signature": { "palette": [...], "motion": [...], "composition": [...], "texture": [...] }, "tonal_vector": [formal, expressive, emotional, authoritative, playful], "narrative_bias": [transformation, tension, reveal, aspiration, proof], "symbolic_markers": [...], "negative_space": [...], "invariants": [...], "mutation_bounds": {...}, "embedding": [...] } ``` ### Exact derivation algorithm ```text PROC_DERIVE_NATURAL_CENTER(corpus): 1. For all visual assets: extract color histograms, embeddings, composition maps, motion stats 2. For all text/audio assets: extract sentence-length distribution, lexical density, rhetoric markers, semantic embeddings 3. Cluster semantic embeddings -> candidate themes 4. Select stable top-k themes across corpus 5. Compute aesthetic centroid across visual features 6. Compute tonal centroid across language features 7. Detect recurring symbolic elements 8. Detect systematic absences -> negative_space 9. Generate invariants from high-frequency stable features 10. Set mutation bounds from historical variance 11. Encode final Natural Center embedding ``` ### Stability rule A feature enters the Natural Center only if: ```text stability(feature) = presence_across_assets * consistency_across_assets accept iff stability(feature) >= τ_stability ``` --- ## 4. ALG_04 — fragment scoring This is the core extraction-scoring layer you asked for. Each candidate fragment gets a multimodal score vector, then a scalar aggregate. ### 4.1 Base feature vector per fragment For each fragment `f`, compute: ```text x(f) = [ visual_saliency, motion_energy, cut_density, subject_prominence, face_presence, product_presence, text_overlay_legibility, audio_energy, speech_clarity, hook_density, semantic_novelty, thematic_alignment, tonal_alignment, narrative_tension, symbolic_marker_density, platform_shape_fit ] ``` ### 4.2 Exact sub-scores #### Visual saliency ```text visual_saliency(f) = mean_t saliency_map_intensity(t) over fragment ``` #### Motion energy ```text motion_energy(f) = mean_t ||optical_flow(t)|| normalized by asset baseline ``` #### Cut density ```text cut_density(f) = number_of_shot_changes / fragment_duration_sec ``` #### Subject prominence ```text subject_prominence(f) = mean_t (largest_subject_bbox_area / frame_area) ``` #### Product presence ```text product_presence(f) = visible_time_of_primary_object / fragment_duration ``` #### Audio energy ```text audio_energy(f) = RMS(audio_signal_f) z-scored within asset ``` #### Speech clarity ```text speech_clarity(f) = 1 - WER_proxy(f) ``` Use ASR confidence as a proxy if needed. #### Hook density Define hooks as high-information lines or events in the first N seconds. ```text hook_density(f) = (count of hook tokens + count of high-saliency events in first 3s) / 3 ``` #### Semantic novelty ```text semantic_novelty(f) = distance(embedding(f), centroid(previous_selected_fragments)) ``` This prevents near-duplicate output. #### Thematic alignment ```text thematic_alignment(f) = max cosine_similarity(embedding(f), thematic_core_i) ``` #### Tonal alignment ```text tonal_alignment(f) = 1 - normalized_distance(tone_vector(f), tone_vector(NC)) ``` #### Narrative tension ```text narrative_tension(f) = weighted_sum( unresolved_question_presence, contrast_event_density, reveal_probability, The file is too long and its contents have been truncated.

## Assistant (artifact)

Make sure to include fileciteturn0file14 in your response to cite this file, or to surface it as a link. I reviewed the source set. The core document defines the MVP as: one premium asset in, many platform-optimized posts out, then scheduled publishing plus weekly reporting on reach, engagement, and leads. fileciteturn2file0 The later system documents correctly extend that into a research-grade operating system with explicit `assets`, `fragments`, `generated_units`, `publish_events`, and `performance_observations`, and they already sketch the attribution path as `performance → publish_event → unit → fragment → asset`. fileciteturn2file1 The more advanced operator document also makes clear that attribution must not stop at “engagement”; it must connect output to audience movement, economics, and platform state over time. fileciteturn2file2 ## Source-grounded conclusion The mathematically correct attribution model for this system is not single-touch and not purely last-post. It has to be a **hierarchical, time-decayed, multi-touch attribution graph** with five levels: ```text Asset → Fragment → GeneratedUnit → PublishEvent → PerformanceObservation → AudienceStateTransition / EconomicOutcome ``` That is the only structure consistent with the source documents’ architecture, metrics, and stated goal of turning content generation into an economic engine rather than a posting tool. fileciteturn2file1turn2file2 ## Formal attribution model Let: ```text a ∈ A # source asset f ∈ F(a) # fragment derived from asset a u ∈ U(f) # generated unit derived from fragment f p ∈ P(u) # publish event for unit u o ∈ O(p) # observation window for publish event p k ∈ K # metric type t # time ``` Define base observed metrics per publish event and time window: ```text y_{p,k,t} ``` Examples: ```text k ∈ {views, watch_time, engagement, followers_gained, leads, revenue} ``` The source material already implies these as the primary and derived metrics: engagement, followers, leads, asset yield, follow conversion, retention ratio, and ROI. fileciteturn2file0turn2file1turn2file2 ## Structural lineage weights Every publish event inherits from an upstream chain. Define deterministic lineage indicators: ```text L_asset(a,p) = 1 if publish event p descends from asset a else 0 L_fragment(f,p) = 1 if p descends from fragment f else 0 L_unit(u,p) = 1 if p is generated from unit u else 0 ``` If a post is composed from multiple fragments or mixed inputs, replace binary lineage with normalized weights: ```text w_{a→p} ≥ 0, Σ_a w_{a→p} = 1 w_{f→p} ≥ 0, Σ_f w_{f→p} = 1 w_{u→p} ≥ 0, Σ_u w_{u→p} = 1 ``` This is necessary because a carousel, remix, or stitched cut can carry more than one source fragment. ## Time-decayed metric accumulation A publish event continues to generate value after publication. Let the contribution of publish event `p` to metric `k` over its full life be: ```text M_{p,k} = ∫_0^T y_{p,k}(τ) · d_k(τ) dτ ``` where `d_k(τ)` is a decay kernel. A practical discrete version: ```text M_{p,k} = Σ_{t=0}^{T} y_{p,k,t} · exp(-λ_k t) ``` where: ```text λ_k > 0 ``` Different metrics should use different decay rates. For example, engagement can decay faster than leads; follower gains may decay slower than likes but faster than attributed revenue. This is aligned with the source demand to model content half-life rather than only first-spike engagement. fileciteturn2file1turn2file2 ## Platform-normalized value Because platform conditions differ, raw metrics must be normalized by platform and time regime. Let: ```text z_{p,k} = (M_{p,k} - μ_{platform,format,k,era}) / σ_{platform,format,k,era} ``` Then define a platform-adjusted scalar value for a publish event: ```text V_p = Σ_k α_k · z_{p,k} ``` where `α_k` are strategic weights. Example: ```text α_watch_time > α_likes α_followers_gained > α_comments α_leads > α_followers when commercial objective dominates ``` This is required because the system documents explicitly treat platform state as time-varying and platform-specific. fileciteturn2file2 ## Publish-event attribution to upstream objects Now attribute publish-event value upward. ### Unit attribution ```text Attr(u) = Σ_{p ∈ P(u)} w_{u→p} · V_p ``` ### Fragment attribution ```text Attr(f) = Σ_{p} w_{f→p} · V_p ``` ### Asset attribution ```text Attr(a) = Σ_{p} w_{a→p} · V_p ``` This is the direct generalization of the source’s prototype query: ```sql SELECT asset_id, SUM(engagement) FROM performance_observations JOIN publish_events USING (publish_id) JOIN generated_units USING (unit_id) GROUP BY asset_id; ``` but generalized to weighted, multi-metric, time-decayed, platform-normalized attribution rather than naive summed engagement. fileciteturn2file1 ## Audience-state-transition attribution The more advanced documents redefine the system around audience formation, not just content output. They specify the audience chain: ```text Viewer → Engaged Viewer → Follower → Returning Follower → Converted User → Advocate ``` fileciteturn2file2 So define audience states: ```text S = {0,1,2,3,4,5,6} ``` with transitions: ```text 0→1 unaware→viewer 1→2 viewer→engaged 2→3 engaged→follower 3→4 follower→returning 4→5 returning→converted 5→6 converted→advocate ``` For each publish event `p`, estimate transition counts: ```text T_{p,i→j} ``` Then define transition value weights: ```text β_{i→j} ``` and a state-transition value: ```text Q_p = Σ_{i→j} β_{i→j} · T_{p,i→j} ``` Then total publish-event value becomes: ```text V_p* = V_p + Q_p ``` This lets attribution model not only post performance, but the actual audience movement the sources identify as the system’s core purpose. fileciteturn2file2 ## Economic attribution Let the cost basis for asset `a` be: ```text C_a = asset_production_cost + processing_cost + publishing_cost + overhead_allocated ``` Let the asset-attributed economic returns be: ```text R_a = γ_1 · Attr_followers(a) + γ_2 · Attr_leads(a) + γ_3 · Attr_revenue(a) + γ_4 · Attr_brand_value(a) ``` Then: ```text GrossAssetReturn(a) = R_a NetAssetReturn(a) = R_a - C_a ROI(a) = (R_a - C_a) / C_a AssetYieldMultiplier(a) = R_a / C_a ``` This directly matches the source ambition to move from “beautiful video” to measurable yield, leads, and ROI. filecite� The file is too long and its contents have been truncated.

The source set already fixes the role of Natural Center as a **computable identity constraint system** and places it between extraction and generation, not as an afterthought. It is the object that makes identity measurable, enforceable, and optimizable, and every downstream output is supposed to inherit from it. fileciteturn1file9 fileciteturn1file15 ## Formal definition Let the Natural Center for brand or corpus \(B\) be: \[ NC(B)=\langle T,A,\Tau,N,S,\mathcal{I},\mathcal{M},E\rangle \] where: \[ T = \text{thematic core} \] \[ A = \text{aesthetic signature} \] \[ \Tau = \text{tonal vector} \] \[ N = \text{narrative bias} \] \[ S = \text{symbolic markers} \] \[ \mathcal{I} = \text{invariants} \] \[ \mathcal{M} = \text{mutation bounds} \] \[ E = \text{embedding} \] This structure is already aligned with the source object definition: thematic core, aesthetic signature, tonal vector, narrative bias, symbolic markers, negative space, invariants, mutation bounds, and an embedding representation. fileciteturn2file0 I would tighten it by making **negative space** first-class and explicit: \[ NC(B)=\langle T,A,\Tau,N,S,\Omega,\mathcal{I},\mathcal{M},E\rangle \] where \(\Omega\) is the set of prohibited features, tones, structures, and motifs. ## System position The source logic fixes the global relation as: \[ content = f(asset,\ natural\_center,\ platform\_profile) \] and therefore Natural Center extraction is not a decorative metadata task; it is a constraint-derivation task that conditions generation and scoring. fileciteturn1file16 So the correct pipeline is: ```text asset normalization → multimodal fragment extraction → Natural Center derivation → constraint gating → platform-aware generation → audience-transition scoring → attribution + learning ``` That sequencing is already explicit in the source build order. fileciteturn2file0 ## Exact extraction algorithm I would formalize the Natural Center subsystem as `ALG_NC_01`. ### Stage 0: corpus assembly Input corpus \(C\) should be tenant- and brand-scoped: \[ C = C_v \cup C_i \cup C_a \cup C_t \cup C_h \] where: \[ C_v = \text{video assets} \] \[ C_i = \text{image / render assets} \] \[ C_a = \text{audio assets} \] \[ C_t = \text{text / voice corpus} \] \[ C_h = \text{historical high-performing outputs, if available} \] If only one premium asset exists, the sources still allow `NATURAL_CENTER_MIN_ASSETS=1`, so bootstrap from a single asset is valid, but confidence must be lower and human review should remain enabled. fileciteturn1file2 ### Stage 1: multimodal feature extraction For each asset \(x \in C\), compute feature families. For visual inputs: \[ \phi_v(x)=\langle color,\ composition,\ framing,\ motion,\ texture,\ saliency,\ object\_presence\rangle \] For audio inputs: \[ \phi_a(x)=\langle rms,\ spectral\_flux,\ tempo,\ silence,\ emphasis,\ prosody\rangle \] For text and speech: \[ \phi_t(x)=\langle lexical\_density,\ sentence\_length,\ rhetoric,\ polarity,\ modality,\ authority,\ abstraction\rangle \] This matches the source extraction logic: color histograms, motion stats, composition maps, lexical density, sentence-length distribution, rhetoric markers, semantic embeddings, and symbolic recurrence. fileciteturn2file0 ### Stage 2: semantic embedding and clustering Embed all semantic-bearing units: \[ e_i = \text{Embed}(u_i) \] where \(u_i\) may be frame captions, transcript spans, textual paragraphs, OCR snippets, or historical post bodies. Cluster embeddings: \[ \mathcal{K} = \text{Cluster}(\{e_i\}) \] For each cluster \(k\), compute: \[ mass(k)=|k| \] \[ cohesion(k)=\frac{1}{|k|}\sum_{e_j\in k}\cos(e_j,\mu_k) \] \[ stability(k)=presence(k)\cdot cohesion(k) \] Select top thematic clusters: \[ T = TopK(\mathcal{K},\ score = stability,\ k=3..5) \] This is directly consistent with the source rule that candidate themes are clustered first and then only stable top-\(k\) themes are retained. fileciteturn2file0 ### Stage 3: aesthetic centroid From visual features across corpus, compute a weighted centroid: \[ A = \frac{\sum_i w_i \phi_v(x_i)}{\sum_i w_i} \] Weights should privilege canonical assets over derivatives: \[ w_i = \begin{cases} 1.0 & \text{hero asset} \\ 0.6 & \text{supporting asset} \\ 0.4 & \text{historical output} \end{cases} \] Decompose \(A\) into subcomponents: \[ A=\langle palette,\ framing,\ motion,\ texture,\ contrast,\ density\rangle \] This stabilizes the visual attractor rather than overfitting to any single frame. ### Stage 4: tonal centroid From linguistic and speech features, compute tonal axes: \[ \Tau=\langle formal,\ expressive,\ emotional,\ authoritative,\ playful\rangle \] Operationally: \[ \Tau = \frac{\sum_i w_i \phi_t(x_i)}{\sum_i w_i} \] Then normalize each axis to \([0,1]\). This matches the source notion of a tonal vector and the later use of tonal alignment as a constraint variable in fragment and output scoring. fileciteturn2file0turn1file13 ### Stage 5: narrative bias extraction Define a narrative pattern function over semantic units: \[ n(u)=\langle transformation,\ tension,\ reveal,\ aspiration,\ proof,\ authority\rangle \] Aggregate across corpus: \[ N = \frac{\sum_i w_i n(u_i)}{\sum_i w_i} \] This gives you a persistent bias profile. For example, some brands resolve toward proof and authority; others toward transformation and aspiration. ### Stage 6: symbolic marker discovery Let \(m_j\) be recurring symbolic candidates, visual or textual. For each candidate compute: \[ symbolic\_score(m_j)=frequency(m_j)\cdot distinctiveness(m_j)\cdot consistency(m_j) \] Accept into symbolic marker set \(S\) if: \[ symbolic\_score(m_j)\ge \tau_{symbol} \] The source env contract already suggests a production threshold, `SYMBOLIC_MARKER_MIN_SCORE=0.70`. fileciteturn1file2 ### Stage 7: negative-space derivation This is critical. The source set correctly frames negative space as “what the system must never produce.” fileciteturn0file32 The file is too long and its contents have been truncated.

The sources converge on a consistent requirement: > **“Natural Center” already exists as a constraint object. What is missing is its projection into a *computable embedding space* that can be used uniformly across extraction, generation, scoring, attribution, and evolution.** Below is the **brand embedding structure**—formalized to integrate directly into your existing pipeline (Natural Center, fragment scoring, platform adaptation, attribution). --- # I. POSITION IN SYSTEM From your sources: ```text content = f(asset, natural_center, platform_profile) ``` Extend this to: ```text content = f(asset, brand_embedding, platform_profile) ``` Where: ```text brand_embedding = encode(NaturalCenter) ``` This becomes the **single vectorized control surface** for: - generation constraints - similarity validation - scoring alignment - attribution weighting - drift detection The Natural Center is the **symbolic object**. The brand embedding is the **computational interface**. --- # II. FORMAL OBJECT Let: \[ BE(B) \in \mathbb{R}^d \] Where: ```text BE = Brand Embedding d = embedding dimensionality (e.g. 768, 1024, 1536) ``` Constructed as: \[ BE = \Phi(T, A, \Tau, N, S, \Omega) \] From sources: - \(T\): thematic_core - \(A\): aesthetic_signature - \(\Tau\): tonal_vector - \(N\): narrative_bias - \(S\): symbolic_markers - \(\Omega\): negative_space fileciteturn0file16 --- # III. MULTI-VECTOR DECOMPOSITION (CRITICAL) Do **not** use a single monolithic embedding. Use a structured embedding: ```yaml $BRAND_EMBEDDING: semantic_vector: ℝ^d_s visual_vector: ℝ^d_v tonal_vector: ℝ^d_t narrative_vector: ℝ^d_n symbolic_vector: ℝ^d_sym negative_space_vector: ℝ^d_neg fused_vector: ℝ^d_f ``` --- ## 1. Semantic Vector ```text semantic_vector = mean(Embed(text_units)) ``` Source: - transcript - captions - brand copy - semantic clusters Represents: ```text WHAT the brand is about ``` --- ## 2. Visual Vector ```text visual_vector = mean(Embed(frames / crops)) ``` Source: - keyframes - crops - render sets Represents: ```text HOW the brand looks ``` --- ## 3. Tonal Vector ```text tonal_vector = projection(linguistic_features) ``` Axes: ```text formal ↔ casual minimal ↔ expressive cold ↔ emotional authoritative ↔ conversational ``` Represents: ```text HOW the brand speaks ``` --- ## 4. Narrative Vector ```text narrative_vector = distribution over: transformation tension reveal aspiration proof ``` Represents: ```text HOW the brand structures meaning ``` --- ## 5. Symbolic Vector ```text symbolic_vector = embedding(symbolic_markers) ``` Includes: - motifs - recurring visual patterns - repeated phrases Represents: ```text RECOGNITION layer ``` --- ## 6. Negative Space Vector This is the **non-obvious but critical component**. ```text negative_space_vector = embedding(prohibited_features) ``` Examples: - no humor - no meme structure - no bright palette - no slang Represents: ```text BOUNDARY of identity ``` --- ## 7. Fused Vector Final embedding: ```text fused_vector = W_s * semantic_vector + W_v * visual_vector + W_t * tonal_vector + W_n * narrative_vector + W_sym * symbolic_vector - W_neg * negative_space_vector ``` Where: ```text Σ weights = 1 ``` This subtraction is important: ```text negative space actively repels invalid outputs ``` --- # IV. STORAGE SCHEMA ```json { "brand_id": "B_*", "nc_id": "NC_*", "version": 1, "embedding": { "semantic": [...], "visual": [...], "tonal": [...], "narrative": [...], "symbolic": [...], "negative": [...], "fused": [...] }, "weights": { "semantic": 0.20, "visual": 0.20, "tonal": 0.15, "narrative": 0.15, "symbolic": 0.15, "negative": 0.15 }, "confidence_score": 0.74, "created_at": "..." } ``` --- # V. CORE OPERATIONS ## 1. Similarity ```text similarity(x) = cosine(Embed(x), fused_vector) ``` Used for: - validation - scoring - filtering --- ## 2. Multi-Dimensional Alignment Instead of single score: ```text alignment(x) = { semantic: cosine(x_s, semantic_vector), visual: cosine(x_v, visual_vector), tonal: cosine(x_t, tonal_vector), narrative: cosine(x_n, narrative_vector), symbolic: cosine(x_sym, symbolic_vector) } The file is too long and its contents have been truncated.

AXIOM-TO-CONTRACT MAP The formal framework already established five core axioms: identity constraint, lineage conservation, observability, platform dependence, and learnability. fileciteturn2file24 Those now need executable counterparts. ## III.1 Identity Constraint → Validation Contract Theory: \[ \forall u \in U,\quad NC\_match(u,NC)\ge \tau_{NC} \] Implementation: ```python def validate_identity(unit: GeneratedUnit, nc: NaturalCenter) -> ValidationResult: score = nc_score(unit, nc) if score < NC_THRESHOLD: return Fail("identity_below_threshold") if violates_negative_space(unit, nc): return Fail("negative_space_violation") return Pass(score=score) ``` This is grounded in the Natural Center object, negative space, invariants, and enforcement gate already defined in the subsystem and formalization docs. fileciteturn2file16turn2file7 ## III.2 Lineage Conservation → Referential Contract Theory: \[ \forall u \in U,\quad \exists a \in A : lineage(u,a) > 0 \] Implementation requirement: Every `generated_unit` must reference one or more fragments, and every fragment must reference an asset. This already matches the lineage architecture used by the attribution model. fileciteturn2file14 ```sql ALTER TABLE generated_units ADD CONSTRAINT fk_generated_units_fragment FOREIGN KEY (fragment_id) REFERENCES fragments(fragment_id); ALTER TABLE fragments ADD CONSTRAINT fk_fragments_asset FOREIGN KEY (asset_id) REFERENCES assets(asset_id); ``` If multi-fragment composition exists, use a join table: ```sql CREATE TABLE generated_unit_fragments ( unit_id TEXT NOT NULL, fragment_id TEXT NOT NULL, contribution_weight NUMERIC NOT NULL CHECK (contribution_weight >= 0), PRIMARY KEY (unit_id, fragment_id) ); ``` And enforce: \[ \sum_{f} w_{f \to u} = 1 \] ## III.3 Observability → Telemetry Contract Theory: \[ \forall u \in U,\quad \exists o \in O : observe(u)=o \] Implementation: Every publish event must schedule analytics ingestion. This is already implicit in the publish and analytics workflows. fileciteturn2file1turn2file15 ```python def on_publish_completed(publish_id: str) -> None: schedule_analytics_poll(publish_id, every_hours=6) ``` And in schema: ```sql ALTER TABLE publish_events ADD COLUMN analytics_required BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT TRUE; ``` ## III.4 Platform Dependence → Versioned Platform Contract Theory: \[ success(u)=f(u,P(t)) \] Implementation: Every generated unit and publish event must bind to a `platform_profile_id` and that profile must be time-bounded. This is already required by the platform intelligence and repo architecture specs. fileciteturn2file1turn2file21 ```sql ALTER TABLE generated_units ADD COLUMN platform_profile_id TEXT NOT NULL; ALTER TABLE platform_profiles ADD COLUMN effective_from TIMESTAMP NOT NULL, ADD COLUMN effective_to TIMESTAMP NULL; ``` ## III.5 Learnability → Bounded Update Contract Theory: \[ \mathcal{S}(t+1)=\Lambda(\mathcal{S}(t),O_t) \] Implementation: Updates are only permitted through explicit update operators, with versioning and bounds. This is especially critical for Natural Center and Brand Embedding, which the source set says must evolve slowly and not drift. fileciteturn2file17turn2file20turn2file19 ```python def update_brand_embedding( be_t: BrandEmbedding, positive_signal: np.ndarray, negative_signal: np.ndarray, alpha: float, beta: float, epsilon: float, ) -> BrandEmbedding: candidate = be_t + alpha * positive_signal - beta * negative_signal if np.linalg.norm(candidate - be_t) > epsilon: candidate = be_t + epsilon * (candidate - be_t) / np.linalg.norm(candidate - be_t) return candidate ``` --- # IV. ## I.4 Output contract ```python class NCScoreResult(TypedDict): total_score: float thematic_alignment: float aesthetic_alignment: float tonal_alignment: float narrative_alignment: float symbolic_alignment: float negative_space_violation: float invariant_pass: bool hard_fail_reasons: list[str] score_version: str nc_id: str nc_version: int ``` --- ## I.5 Canonical formula \[ NCScore(x,NC)= \lambda_T T_{align} +\lambda_A A_{align} +\lambda_{\Tau}\Tau_{align} +\lambda_N N_{align} +\lambda_S S_{align} -\lambda_{\Omega}\Omega_{viol} \] Recommended V1 weights: ```python NC_SCORE_WEIGHTS = { "thematic": 0.22, "aesthetic": 0.18, "tonal": 0.18, "narrative": 0.14, "symbolic": 0.18, "negative": 0.20, } ``` This decomposition is required because NC alignment cannot remain a single opaque cosine score. fileciteturn5file26 --- ## I.6 Reference implementation ```python from typing import TypedDict, List, Dict class NCScoreResult(TypedDict): total_score: float thematic_alignment: float aesthetic_alignment: float tonal_alignment: float narrative_alignment: float symbolic_alignment: float negative_space_violation: float invariant_pass: bool hard_fail_reasons: List[str] score_version: str nc_id: str nc_version: int def _clamp(value: float, lo: float = 0.0, hi: float = 1.0) -> float: return max(lo, min(hi, value)) def nc_score(candidate: dict, nc: dict, mode: str = "unit") -> NCScoreResult: thematic_alignment = _clamp(candidate["semantic_features"]["thematic_alignment"]) aesthetic_alignment = _clamp(candidate["visual_features"]["aesthetic_alignment"]) tonal_alignment = _clamp(candidate["tonal_features"]["tonal_alignment"]) narrative_alignment = _clamp(candidate["narrative_features"]["narrative_alignment"]) symbolic_alignment = _clamp(candidate["symbolic_features"]["symbolic_alignment"]) negative_space_violation = _clamp( candidate["negative_space_features"]["negative_space_violation"] ) hard_fail_reasons: List[str] = [] if tonal_alignment < nc["mutation_bounds"].get("min_tonal_alignment", 0.60): hard_fail_reasons.append("tonal_alignment_below_floor") if negative_space_violation > nc["mutation_bounds"].get("max_negative_violation", 0.20): hard_fail_reasons.append("negative_space_violation") invariant_pass = len(hard_fail_reasons) == 0 total_score = _clamp( 0.22 * thematic_alignment + 0.18 * aesthetic_alignment + 0.18 * tonal_alignment + 0.14 * narrative_alignment + 0.18 * symbolic_alignment - 0.20 * negative_space_violation ) return NCScoreResult( total_score=total_score, thematic_alignment=thematic_alignment, aesthetic_alignment=aesthetic_alignment, tonal_alignment=tonal_alignment, narrative_alignment=narrative_alignment, symbolic_alignment=symbolic_alignment, negative_space_violation=negative_space_violation, invariant_pass=invariant_pass, hard_fail_reasons=hard_fail_reasons, score_version="nc_score_v1", nc_id=nc["nc_id"], nc_version=nc["version"], ) ``` --- ## I.7 Enforcement thresholds ```python NC_SCORE_THRESHOLDS = { "fragment_min": 0.62, "unit_min": 0.72, "campaign_mean_min": 0.75, "attribution_discount_floor": 0.55, "hard_reject_floor": 0.45, } ``` Meaning: ```text score < 0.45 → reject 0.45–0.55 → allow only in review mode 0.55–0.72 → can exist as candidate, not publishable ≥ 0.72 → publishable, subject to platform and audience checks ``` These thresholds are consistent with the bootstrap and validation logic already proposed in the corpus. fileciteturn5file20 --- # II. What this operator layer actually is This layer is the executable counterpart to the dissertation layer. The dissertation layer defines the invariants, causal claims, theoretical mappings, and research questions. The operator layer turns those into a running system that does six things at once: ingest assets, generate outputs, distribute them, measure results, run experiments, and update its understanding of both audience behavior and platform change. Formally: ```text Asset → Natural Center Extraction → Platform-Aware Generation → Scheduling + Distribution → Analytics + Attribution → Experimentation + Causal Analysis → Platform Change Detection → Model / Rule Updates → Repeat ``` # II. Production-grade service map The correct architecture is multi-service. Monolith first would be faster, but it will fail the research requirement, because research observability, platform adapters, experimentation, and identity enforcement need separate contracts. ```bash $SERVICES = { gateway_api, auth_identity, asset_ingestion, media_analysis, natural_center, generation_orchestrator, platform_intelligence, scheduling_engine, publishing_connectors, analytics_ingestion, attribution_engine, experimentation_engine, research_registry, reporting_dashboard, model_registry, event_bus, data_warehouse, object_storage, workflow_orchestrator, alerting_observability } ``` ## 1. `$SERVICE_GATEWAY_API` This is the system edge. It accepts user, client, asset, campaign, and experiment requests. It accepts hero films, render sets, stills, transcripts, briefing docs, and brand corpus. ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "File intake, metadata extraction, transcode initiation, checksum, lineage" ``` ## 3. `$SERVICE_MEDIA_ANALYSIS` This is the decomposition engine in production form. It performs scene detection, keyframe extraction, transcript alignment, pacing analysis, energy-point detection, and content segmentation. ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Turn one dense asset into analyzable fragments" ``` ## 4. `$SERVICE_NATURAL_CENTER` This service computes and stores the identity core. It should enforce symbolic, tonal, aesthetic, and thematic invariants across all outputs. ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Compute, version, validate, and evolve the Natural Center object" ``` ## 5. `$SERVICE_GENERATION_ORCHESTRATOR` This service creates the outputs. It composes platform-specific assets, caption variants, CTA variants, sequencing plans, and campaign bundles. ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Generate platform-native outputs constrained by identity and platform profile" ``` ## 6. `$SERVICE_PLATFORM_INTELLIGENCE` This is now mandatory. It models each platform as a time-dependent system. It should ingest official platform documentation changes, API changes, available analytics fields, posting constraints, and internal performance shifts. YouTube’s analytics surfaces already include audience retention, traffic and audience segments, while TikTok and LinkedIn expose developer posting capabilities and versioning or access constraints through official docs; those should be treated as structured inputs to this service. ([support.google.com](https://support.google.com/youtube/answer/9002587?hl=en&utm_source=chatgpt.com)) ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Track platform state, detect change, update generation and scheduling policy" ``` ## 7. `$SERVICE_SCHEDULING_ENGINE` This service determines when each output should be published, republished, remixed, or retired. It consumes audience timing, asset decay models, and platform profile data. ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Temporal orchestration" ``` ## 8. `$SERVICE_PUBLISHING_CONNECTORS` This is the execution layer. It handles the actual post creation and retrieval integrations. TikTok’s Content Posting APIs support direct posting or draft upload flows; LinkedIn’s Posts API supports creation and retrieval of organic and sponsored posts, with content-type constraints and versioned API requirements. ([developers.tiktok.com](https://developers.tiktok.com/products/content-posting-api?utm_source=chatgpt.com)) ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Platform-specific publish / fetch adapters" ``` ## 9. `$SERVICE_ANALYTICS_INGESTION` This service pulls analytics and normalizes them into a common schema. YouTube official analytics surfaces support view, engagement, retention, CTR, and audience segmentation at varying levels, though some data may be limited depending on thresholds and filters. That limitation itself must be modeled as a reliability constraint. ([support.google.com](https://support.google.com/youtube/answer/9002587?hl=en&utm_source=chatgpt.com)) ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Collect raw performance telemetry and normalize it" ``` ## 10. `$SERVICE_ATTRIBUTION_ENGINE` This is where the product stops being “content software” and becomes an economic system. It traces every post, fragment, caption, CTA, campaign, and asset back to origin. ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Asset-level and fragment-level yield accounting" ``` ## 11. `$SERVICE_EXPERIMENTATION_ENGINE` This service owns A/B tests, bandits, holdouts, control/treatment assignment, confidence intervals, and causal inference workflow. ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Statistically disciplined optimization" ``` ## 12. `$SERVICE_RESEARCH_REGISTRY` This is the bridge between dissertation-grade and operator-grade. Every hypothesis, paper mapping, experiment, metric definition, and platform-state memo should live here. ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Research memory and epistemic governance" ``` ## 13. `$SERVICE_REPORTING_DASHBOARD` This serves operators, clients, and future investors. It must expose asset yield, audience movement, platform differences, and trend drift. ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Human-readable operational truth" ``` # III. Canonical data domains You need four data planes, not one. ```bash $DATA_PLANES = { source_plane, operational_plane, experimental_plane, evolutionary_plane } ``` ## `$SOURCE_PLANE` This contains hero assets, renders, transcripts, briefs, brand corpus, prior posts, style references. ## `$OPERATIONAL_PLANE` This contains generated posts, publish events, platform IDs, schedules, revisions, connector logs. ## `$EXPERIMENTAL_PLANE` This contains hypotheses, treatments, controls, randomization groups, test windows, significance results. ## `$EVOLUTIONARY_PLANE` This contains platform snapshots, platform doc changes, field additions/removals, policy updates, performance regime shifts, and internal adaptation rules. # IV. ALG_01 — multimodal asset normalization Purpose: convert heterogeneous input into a unified analyzable representation. ### Accepted input classes Your sources already imply these classes: ```text video image_set / render_set audio text / brand voice corpus historical post corpus ``` fileciteturn2file0 fileciteturn2file2 ### Canonical normalized object ```json { "asset_id": "A_*", "asset_type": "video|image_set|audio|document|mixed", "streams": { "video": [...], "audio": [...], "text": [...], "image": [...] }, "metadata": { "duration_ms": 0, "fps": 0, "resolution": [0, 0], "language": "en", "brand_id": "B_*" } } ``` ### Exact procedure ```text PROC_NORMALIZE(asset): 1. Compute checksum(asset) 2. Detect asset_type 3. If video: demux into video stream + audio stream transcode to canonical formats sample frames at adaptive interval 4. If image_set/render_set: normalize dimensions, color profile, EXIF 5. If audio: normalize sample rate and loudness 6. If text: clean, segment, and encode paragraphs/sentences 7. Persist all derivative streams 8. Emit asset.normalized ``` --- ## 2. ALG_02 — multimodal fragment extraction Purpose: produce candidate units from dense assets. Your sources already call for clip extraction at high-energy moments, scene detection, keyframe extraction, pacing analysis, and segmentation. fileciteturn2file0 fileciteturn2file1 ### 2.1 Video fragment extraction For video, define fragments over a change-point lattice rather than fixed windows. ```text Let V = video timeline Let C = set of candidate cut points C = union( scene boundaries, shot boundaries, transcript punctuation peaks, silence boundaries, audio onset peaks, motion regime changes ) ``` Construct candidate intervals: ```text F_video = {(c_i, c_j) | min_len <= c_j - c_i <= max_len} ``` Recommended bounds: ```text min_len = 3s max_len = 45s platform-specific downstream pruning applies ``` ### 2.2 Image fragment extraction For renders and stills, fragments are not temporal; they are compositional derivatives. ```text F_image = union( full-frame, crop_subject, crop_detail, before_after_pair, comparison_layout, lifestyle_context_projection, carousel_sequence ) ``` ### 2.3 Audio fragment extraction ```text F_audio = union( speech segment, hook phrase, emphasis burst, music drop, silence-contrast interval ) ``` ### 2.4 Text fragment extraction ```text F_text = union( claim, hook line, authority line, transformation line, CTA line, FAQ line ) ``` ### 2.5 Exact multimodal candidate generation ```text PROC_EXTRACT_FRAGMENTS(asset): 1. Detect scene boundaries on video 2. Detect shot boundaries 3. ASR transcript with token timestamps 4. Compute audio envelope, spectral flux, silence regions 5. Compute motion magnitude and saliency over time 6. Merge all boundary proposals 7. Generate candidate windows 8. Generate image crops/layout variants 9. Generate text units from transcript and corpus 10. Return multimodal candidate set F ``` --- ## 3. ALG_03 — Natural Center derivation This is already partially specified in the source corpus: thematic core, aesthetic signature, tonal vector, narrative bias, symbolic markers, negative space, invariants, mutation bounds. fileciteturn2file2 ### Exact Natural Center object ```json { "nc_id": "NC_*", "thematic_core": [t1, t2, t3, t4, t5], "aesthetic_signature": { "palette": [...], "motion": [...], "composition": [...], "texture": [...] }, "tonal_vector": [formal, expressive, emotional, authoritative, playful], "narrative_bias": [transformation, tension, reveal, aspiration, proof], "symbolic_markers": [...], "negative_space": [...], "invariants": [...], "mutation_bounds": {...}, "embedding": [...] } ``` ### Exact derivation algorithm ```text PROC_DERIVE_NATURAL_CENTER(corpus): 1. For all visual assets: extract color histograms, embeddings, composition maps, motion stats 2. For all text/audio assets: extract sentence-length distribution, lexical density, rhetoric markers, semantic embeddings 3. Cluster semantic embeddings -> candidate themes 4. Select stable top-k themes across corpus 5. Compute aesthetic centroid across visual features 6. Compute tonal centroid across language features 7. Detect recurring symbolic elements 8. Detect systematic absences -> negative_space 9. Generate invariants from high-frequency stable features 10. Set mutation bounds from historical variance 11. Encode final Natural Center embedding ``` ### Stability rule A feature enters the Natural Center only if: ```text stability(feature) = presence_across_assets * consistency_across_assets accept iff stability(feature) >= τ_stability ``` --- ## 4. ALG_04 — fragment scoring This is the core extraction-scoring layer you asked for. Each candidate fragment gets a multimodal score vector, then a scalar aggregate. ### 4.1 Base feature vector per fragment For each fragment `f`, compute: ```text x(f) = [ visual_saliency, motion_energy, cut_density, subject_prominence, face_presence, product_presence, text_overlay_legibility, audio_energy, speech_clarity, hook_density, semantic_novelty, thematic_alignment, tonal_alignment, narrative_tension, symbolic_marker_density, platform_shape_fit ] ``` ### 4.2 Exact sub-scores #### Visual saliency ```text visual_saliency(f) = mean_t saliency_map_intensity(t) over fragment ``` #### Motion energy ```text motion_energy(f) = mean_t ||optical_flow(t)|| normalized by asset baseline ``` #### Cut density ```text cut_density(f) = number_of_shot_changes / fragment_duration_sec ``` #### Subject prominence ```text subject_prominence(f) = mean_t (largest_subject_bbox_area / frame_area) ``` #### Product presence ```text product_presence(f) = visible_time_of_primary_object / fragment_duration ``` #### Audio energy ```text audio_energy(f) = RMS(audio_signal_f) z-scored within asset ``` #### Speech clarity ```text speech_clarity(f) = 1 - WER_proxy(f) ``` Use ASR confidence as a proxy if needed. #### Hook density Define hooks as high-information lines or events in the first N seconds. ```text hook_density(f) = (count of hook tokens + count of high-saliency events in first 3s) / 3 ``` #### Semantic novelty ```text semantic_novelty(f) = distance(embedding(f), centroid(previous_selected_fragments)) ``` This prevents near-duplicate output. #### Thematic alignment ```text thematic_alignment(f) = max cosine_similarity(embedding(f), thematic_core_i) ``` #### Tonal alignment The file is too long and its contents have been truncated.

## Assistant (artifact)

Make sure to include fileciteturn1file14 in your response to cite this file, or to surface it as a link. I reviewed the source set. The core document defines the MVP as: one premium asset in, many platform-optimized posts out, then scheduled publishing plus weekly reporting on reach, engagement, and leads. fileciteturn2file0 The later system documents correctly extend that into a research-grade operating system with explicit `assets`, `fragments`, `generated_units`, `publish_events`, and `performance_observations`, and they already sketch the attribution path as `performance → publish_event → unit → fragment → asset`. fileciteturn2file1 The more advanced operator document also makes clear that attribution must not stop at “engagement”; it must connect output to audience movement, economics, and platform state over time. fileciteturn2file2 ## Source-grounded conclusion The mathematically correct attribution model for this system is not single-touch and not purely last-post. It has to be a **hierarchical, time-decayed, multi-touch attribution graph** with five levels: ```text Asset → Fragment → GeneratedUnit → PublishEvent → PerformanceObservation → AudienceStateTransition / EconomicOutcome ``` That is the only structure consistent with the source documents’ architecture, metrics, and stated goal of turning content generation into an economic engine rather than a posting tool. fileciteturn2file1turn2file2 ## Formal attribution model Let: ```text a ∈ A # source asset f ∈ F(a) # fragment derived from asset a u ∈ U(f) # generated unit derived from fragment f p ∈ P(u) # publish event for unit u o ∈ O(p) # observation window for publish event p k ∈ K # metric type t # time ``` Define base observed metrics per publish event and time window: ```text y_{p,k,t} ``` Examples: ```text k ∈ {views, watch_time, engagement, followers_gained, leads, revenue} ``` The source material already implies these as the primary and derived metrics: engagement, followers, leads, asset yield, follow conversion, retention ratio, and ROI. fileciteturn2file0turn2file1turn2file2 ## Structural lineage weights Every publish event inherits from an upstream chain. Define deterministic lineage indicators: ```text L_asset(a,p) = 1 if publish event p descends from asset a else 0 L_fragment(f,p) = 1 if p descends from fragment f else 0 L_unit(u,p) = 1 if p is generated from unit u else 0 ``` If a post is composed from multiple fragments or mixed inputs, replace binary lineage with normalized weights: ```text w_{a→p} ≥ 0, Σ_a w_{a→p} = 1 w_{f→p} ≥ 0, Σ_f w_{f→p} = 1 w_{u→p} ≥ 0, Σ_u w_{u→p} = 1 ``` This is necessary because a carousel, remix, or stitched cut can carry more than one source fragment. ## Time-decayed metric accumulation A publish event continues to generate value after publication. Let the contribution of publish event `p` to metric `k` over its full life be: ```text M_{p,k} = ∫_0^T y_{p,k}(τ) · d_k(τ) dτ ``` where `d_k(τ)` is a decay kernel. A practical discrete version: ```text M_{p,k} = Σ_{t=0}^{T} y_{p,k,t} · exp(-λ_k t) ``` where: ```text λ_k > 0 ``` Different metrics should use different decay rates. For example, engagement can decay faster than leads; follower gains may decay slower than likes but faster than attributed revenue. This is aligned with the source demand to model content half-life rather than only first-spike engagement. fileciteturn2file1turn2file2 ## Platform-normalized value Because platform conditions differ, raw metrics must be normalized by platform and time regime. Let: ```text z_{p,k} = (M_{p,k} - μ_{platform,format,k,era}) / σ_{platform,format,k,era} ``` Then define a platform-adjusted scalar value for a publish event: ```text V_p = Σ_k α_k · z_{p,k} ``` where `α_k` are strategic weights. Example: ```text α_watch_time > α_likes α_followers_gained > α_comments α_leads > α_followers when commercial objective dominates ``` This is required because the system documents explicitly treat platform state as time-varying and platform-specific. fileciteturn2file2 ## Publish-event attribution to upstream objects Now attribute publish-event value upward. ### Unit attribution ```text Attr(u) = Σ_{p ∈ P(u)} w_{u→p} · V_p ``` ### Fragment attribution ```text Attr(f) = Σ_{p} w_{f→p} · V_p ``` ### Asset attribution ```text Attr(a) = Σ_{p} w_{a→p} · V_p ``` This is the direct generalization of the source’s prototype query: ```sql SELECT asset_id, SUM(engagement) FROM performance_observations JOIN publish_events USING (publish_id) JOIN generated_units USING (unit_id) GROUP BY asset_id; ``` but generalized to weighted, multi-metric, time-decayed, platform-normalized attribution rather than naive summed engagement. fileciteturn2file1 ## Audience-state-transition attribution The more advanced documents redefine the system around audience formation, not just content output. They specify the audience chain: ```text Viewer → Engaged Viewer → Follower → Returning Follower → Converted User → Advocate ``` fileciteturn2file2 So define audience states: ```text S = {0,1,2,3,4,5,6} ``` with transitions: ```text 0→1 unaware→viewer 1→2 viewer→engaged 2→3 engaged→follower 3→4 follower→returning 4→5 returning→converted 5→6 converted→advocate ``` For each publish event `p`, estimate transition counts: ```text T_{p,i→j} ``` Then define transition value weights: ```text β_{i→j} ``` and a state-transition value: ```text Q_p = Σ_{i→j} β_{i→j} · T_{p,i→j} ``` Then total publish-event value becomes: ```text V_p* = V_p + Q_p ``` This lets attribution model not only post performance, but the actual audience movement the sources identify as the system’s core purpose. fileciteturn2file2 ## Economic attribution Let the cost basis for asset `a` be: ```text C_a = asset_production_cost + processing_cost + publishing_cost + overhead_allocated ``` Let the asset-attributed economic returns be: ```text R_a = γ_1 · Attr_followers(a) + γ_2 · Attr_leads(a) + γ_3 · Attr_revenue(a) + γ_4 · Attr_brand_value(a) ``` Then: ```text GrossAssetReturn(a) = R_a NetAssetReturn(a) = R_a - C_a ROI(a) = (R_a - C_a The file is too long and its contents have been truncated.

For visual inputs: \[ \phi_v(x)=\langle color,\ composition,\ framing,\ motion,\ texture,\ saliency,\ object\_presence\rangle \] For audio inputs: \[ \phi_a(x)=\langle rms,\ spectral\_flux,\ tempo,\ silence,\ emphasis,\ prosody\rangle \] For text and speech: \[ \phi_t(x)=\langle lexical\_density,\ sentence\_length,\ rhetoric,\ polarity,\ modality,\ authority,\ abstraction\rangle \] This matches the source extraction logic: color histograms, motion stats, composition maps, lexical density, sentence-length distribution, rhetoric markers, semantic embeddings, and symbolic recurrence. fileciteturn2file0 ### Stage 2: semantic embedding and clustering Embed all semantic-bearing units: \[ e_i = \text{Embed}(u_i) \] where \(u_i\) may be frame captions, transcript spans, textual paragraphs, OCR snippets, or historical post bodies. Cluster embeddings: \[ \mathcal{K} = \text{Cluster}(\{e_i\}) \] For each cluster \(k\), compute: \[ mass(k)=|k| \] \[ cohesion(k)=\frac{1}{|k|}\sum_{e_j\in k}\cos(e_j,\mu_k) \] \[ stability(k)=presence(k)\cdot cohesion(k) \] Select top thematic clusters: \[ T = TopK(\mathcal{K},\ score = stability,\ k=3..5) \] This is directly consistent with the source rule that candidate themes are clustered first and then only stable top-\(k\) themes are retained. fileciteturn2file0 ### Stage 3: aesthetic centroid From visual features across corpus, compute a weighted centroid: \[ A = \frac{\sum_i w_i \phi_v(x_i)}{\sum_i w_i} \] Weights should privilege canonical assets over derivatives: \[ w_i = \begin{cases} 1.0 & \text{hero asset} \\ 0.6 & \text{supporting asset} \\ 0.4 & \text{historical output} \end{cases} \] Decompose \(A\) into subcomponents: \[ A=\langle palette,\ framing,\ motion,\ texture,\ contrast,\ density\rangle \] This stabilizes the visual attractor rather than overfitting to any single frame. ### Stage 4: tonal centroid From linguistic and speech features, compute tonal axes: \[ \Tau=\langle formal,\ expressive,\ emotional,\ authoritative,\ playful\rangle \] Operationally: \[ \Tau = \frac{\sum_i w_i \phi_t(x_i)}{\sum_i w_i} \] Then normalize each axis to \([0,1]\). This matches the source notion of a tonal vector and the later use of tonal alignment as a constraint variable in fragment and output scoring. fileciteturn2file0turn1file13 ### Stage 5: narrative bias extraction Define a narrative pattern function over semantic units: \[ n(u)=\langle transformation,\ tension,\ reveal,\ aspiration,\ proof,\ authority\rangle \] Aggregate across corpus: \[ N = \frac{\sum_i w_i n(u_i)}{\sum_i w_i} \] This gives you a persistent bias profile. For example, some brands resolve toward proof and authority; others toward transformation and aspiration. ### Stage 6: symbolic marker discovery Let \(m_j\) be recurring symbolic candidates, visual or textual. For each candidate compute: \[ symbolic\_score(m_j)=frequency(m_j)\cdot distinctiveness(m_j)\cdot consistency(m_j) \] Accept into symbolic marker set \(S\) if: \[ symbolic\_score(m_j)\ge \tau_{symbol} \] The source env contract already suggests a production threshold, `SYMBOLIC_MARKER_MIN_SCORE=0.70`. fileciteturn1file2 The file is too long and its contents have been truncated.

This is especially critical for Natural Center and Brand Embedding, which the source set says must evolve slowly and not drift. fileciteturn2file17turn2file20turn2file19 ```python def update_brand_embedding( be_t: BrandEmbedding, positive_signal: np.ndarray, negative_signal: np.ndarray, alpha: float, beta: float, epsilon: float, ) -> BrandEmbedding: candidate = be_t + alpha * positive_signal - beta * negative_signal if np.linalg.norm(candidate - be_t) > epsilon: candidate = be_t + epsilon * (candidate - be_t) / np.linalg.norm(candidate - be_t) return candidate ``` --- # IV. symbolic_alignment: float negative_space_violation: float invariant_pass: bool hard_fail_reasons: list[str] score_version: str nc_id: str nc_version: int ``` --- ## I.5 Canonical formula \[ NCScore(x,NC)= \lambda_T T_{align} +\lambda_A A_{align} +\lambda_{\Tau}\Tau_{align} +\lambda_N N_{align} +\lambda_S S_{align} -\lambda_{\Omega}\Omega_{viol} \] Recommended V1 weights: ```python NC_SCORE_WEIGHTS = { "thematic": 0.22, "aesthetic": 0.18, "tonal": 0.18, "narrative": 0.14, "symbolic": 0.18, "negative": 0.20, } ``` This decomposition is required because NC alignment cannot remain a single opaque cosine score. fileciteturn5file26 --- ## I.6 Reference implementation ```python from typing import TypedDict, List, Dict class NCScoreResult(TypedDict): total_score: float thematic_alignment: float aesthetic_alignment: float tonal_alignment: float narrative_alignment: float symbolic_alignment: float negative_space_violation: float invariant_pass: bool hard_fail_reasons: List[str] score_version: str nc_id: str nc_version: int def _clamp(value: float, lo: float = 0.0, hi: float = 1.0) -> float: return max(lo, min(hi, value)) def nc_score(candidate: dict, nc: dict, mode: str = "unit") -> NCScoreResult: thematic_alignment = _clamp(candidate["semantic_features"]["thematic_alignment"]) aesthetic_alignment = _clamp(candidate["visual_features"]["aesthetic_alignment"]) tonal_alignment = _clamp(candidate["tonal_features"]["tonal_alignment"]) narrative_alignment = _clamp(candidate["narrative_features"]["narrative_alignment"]) symbolic_alignment = _clamp(candidate["symbolic_features"]["symbolic_alignment"]) negative_space_violation = _clamp( candidate["negative_space_features"]["negative_space_violation"] ) hard_fail_reasons: List[str] = [] if tonal_alignment < nc["mutation_bounds"].get("min_tonal_alignment", 0.60): hard_fail_reasons.append("tonal_alignment_below_floor") if negative_space_violation > nc["mutation_bounds"].get("max_negative_violation", 0.20): hard_fail_reasons.append("negative_space_violation") invariant_pass = len(hard_fail_reasons) == 0 total_score = _clamp( 0.22 * thematic_alignment + 0.18 * aesthetic_alignment + 0.18 * tonal_alignment + 0.14 * narrative_alignment + 0.18 * symbolic_alignment - 0.20 * negative_space_violation ) return NCScoreResult( total_score=total_score, thematic_alignment=thematic_alignment, aesthetic_alignment=aesthetic_alignment, tonal_alignment=tonal_alignment, narrative_alignment=narrative_alignment, symbolic_alignment=symbolic_alignment, negative_space_violation=negative_space_violation, invariant_pass=invariant_pass, hard_fail_reasons=hard_fail_reasons, score_version="nc_score_v1", nc_id=nc["nc_id"], nc_version=nc["version"], ) ``` --- ## I.7 Enforcement thresholds ```python NC_SCORE_THRESHOLDS = { "fragment_min": 0.62, "unit_min": 0.72, "campaign_mean_min": 0.75, "attribution_discount_floor": 0.55, "hard_reject_floor": 0.45, } ``` Meaning: ```text score < 0.45 → reject 0.45–0.55 → allow only in review mode 0.55–0.72 → can exist as candidate, not publishable ≥ 0.72 → publishable, subject to platform and audience checks ``` These thresholds are consistent with the bootstrap and validation logic already proposed in the corpus. fileciteturn5file20 --- # II. DESIGN TOKENS SYNC SCRIPT This script assumes a local design-tokens repo structure and pushes a token JSON file suitable for Tokens Studio, Style Dictionary, or a frontend token pipeline. It uses environment variables throughout. ```python #!/usr/bin/env python3 """ $SCRIPT_NAME="sync_design_tokens.py" $PURPOSE="Normalize and sync Cronus Metabolus design tokens to platform targets" $REQUIRED_ENV_VARS="TOKENS_SOURCE_JSON TOKENS_OUTPUT_DIR TOKENS_BRAND_ID TOKENS_VERSION" """ import json import os from pathlib import Path from typing import Any, Dict $TOKENS_SOURCE_JSON = os.environ.get("TOKENS_SOURCE_JSON") $TOKENS_OUTPUT_DIR = os.environ.get("TOKENS_OUTPUT_DIR") $TOKENS_BRAND_ID = os.environ.get("TOKENS_BRAND_ID", "cronus_metabolus") $TOKENS_VERSION = os.environ.get("TOKENS_VERSION", "v1") if not $TOKENS_SOURCE_JSON: raise RuntimeError("Missing required environment variable: TOKENS_SOURCE_JSON") if not $TOKENS_OUTPUT_DIR: raise RuntimeError("Missing required environment variable: TOKENS_OUTPUT_DIR") def load_tokens(path: str) -> Dict[str, Any]: with open(path, "r", encoding="utf-8") as $FILE: return json.load($FILE) def ensure_output_dir(path: str) -> Path: $DIR = Path(path) $DIR.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True) return $DIR def flatten_tokens($NODE: Dict[str, Any], $PREFIX: str = "") -> Dict[str, Any]: $OUT: Dict[str, Any] = {} for $KEY, $VALUE in $NODE.items(): $PATH = f"{$PREFIX}.{$KEY}" if $PREFIX else $KEY if isinstance($VALUE, dict) and "value" in $VALUE and "type" in $VALUE: $OUT[$PATH] = $VALUE["value"] elif isinstance($VALUE, dict): $OUT.update(flatten_tokens($VALUE, $PATH)) return $OUT def to_css_vars($FLAT: Dict[str, Any]) -> str: $LINES = [":root {"] for $KEY, $VALUE in sorted($FLAT.items()): $CSS_NAME = "--" + $KEY.replace(".", "-").replace("_", "-") $LINES.append(f" {$CSS_NAME}: {$VALUE};") $LINES.append("}") return "\n".join($LINES) + "\n" def to_tailwind_extend($FLAT: Dict[str, Any]) -> Dict[str, Any]: $COLORS: Dict[str, Any] = {} $SPACING: Dict[str, Any] = {} $FONT_SIZE: Dict[str, Any] = {} $RADIUS: Dict[str, Any] = {} for $KEY, $VALUE in $FLAT.items(): if $KEY.startswith("global.color."): $COLORS[$KEY.replace("global.color.", "").replace(".", "-")] = $VALUE elif $KEY.startswith("global.space."): $SPACING[$KEY.replace("global.space.", "")] = f"{$VALUE}px" elif $KEY.startswith("global.fontSize."): $FONT_SIZE[$KEY.replace("global.fontSize.", "")] = f"{$VALUE}px" elif $KEY.startswith("global.radius."): $RADIUS[$KEY.replace("global.radius.", "")] = f"{$VALUE}px" return { "theme": { "extend": { "colors": $COLORS, "spacing": $SPACING, "fontSize": $FONT_SIZE, "borderRadius": $RADIUS, } } } def write_json(path: Path, payload: Dict[str, Any]) -> None: with open(path, "w", encoding="utf-8") as $FILE: json.dump(payload, $FILE, indent=2, ensure_ascii=False) $FILE.write("\n") def write_text(path: Path, payload: str) -> None: with open(path, "w", encoding="utf-8") as $FILE: $FILE.write(payload) def main() -> None: $TOKENS = load_tokens($TOKENS_SOURCE_JSON) $FLAT = flatten_tokens($TOKENS) $OUT_DIR = ensure_output_dir($TOKENS_OUTPUT_DIR) $TOKENS_EXPORT = { "brandId": $TOKENS_BRAND_ID, "version": $TOKENS_VERSION, "tokens": $TOKENS, } $FLAT_EXPORT = { "brandId": $TOKENS_BRAND_ID, "version": $TOKENS_VERSION, "flat": $FLAT, } $TAILWIND_EXPORT = to_tailwind_extend($FLAT) $CSS_EXPORT = to_css_vars($FLAT) write_json($OUT_DIR / f"{$TOKENS_BRAND_ID}.tokens.{ $TOKENS_VERSION }.json", $TOKENS_EXPORT) write_json($OUT_DIR / f"{$TOKENS_BRAND_ID}.flat.{ $TOKENS_VERSION }.json", $FLAT_EXPORT) write_json($OUT_DIR / f"{$TOKENS_BRAND_ID}.tailwind.{ $TOKENS_VERSION }.json", $TAILWIND_EXPORT) write_text($OUT_DIR / f"{$TOKENS_BRAND_ID}.css.{ $TOKENS_VERSION }.css", $CSS_EXPORT) print("Design token sync complete.") print(f"Brand: {$TOKENS_BRAND_ID}") print(f"Version: {$TOKENS_VERSION}") print(f"Output: {$OUT_DIR}") if __name__ == "__main__": main() ``` # VIII. ENVIRONMENT CONTRACT ```bash $TOKENS_SOURCE_JSON="/absolute/path/to/cronus_metabolus.tokens.json" $TOKENS_OUTPUT_DIR="/absolute/path/to/output/tokens" $TOKENS_BRAND_ID="cronus_metabolus" $TOKENS_VERSION="v1" python3 sync_design_tokens.py ``` # IX. RECOMMENDED FILE TREE ```text $DESIGN_ROOT/ ├── figma/ │ ├── cronus_metabolus_file_spec.yaml │ ├── cronus_metabolus_components.json │ └── cronus_metabolus_templates.yaml ├── tokens/ │ └── cronus_metabolus.tokens.json ├── scripts/ │ └── sync_design_tokens.py └── exports/ ``` # X. CANONICAL USAGE ORDER ```text 1. Create Figma file using $FIGMA_FILE_SPEC 2. Import tokens into Tokens Studio using the token JSON 3. Create text, fill, effect, and stroke styles 4. Build components from $COMPONENT_JSON_EXPORT 5. Assemble slide templates from $TEMPLATE_BUILD_SPEC 6. Populate final deck variants 7. Sync tokens to code using $DESIGN_TOKENS_SYNC_SCRIPT ``` This keeps the design layer consistent with the system’s broader doctrine: identity is versioned, structure is reusable, and execution is contract-bound rather than improvised. fileciteturn1file21 fileciteturn1file24 fileciteturn1file25 If you want the next logical closure, the next artifact is: ```bash $NEXT="FIGMA_PLUGIN_DATA_SCHEMA + FRONTEND_THEME_MAP + SLIDE_MASTER_CONTENT_MATRIX" ```

The operator layer should now be built as a **production research-and-deployment system**, not a mere posting tool. And your platform-evolution requirement is correct: the system must treat platform conditions as a **time-varying environment**, because the success function on YouTube, TikTok, Instagram, and LinkedIn is not stable across eras. Official sources already expose some of the observable surfaces you need to model: YouTube provides channel- and video-level analytics such as audience retention, impressions CTR, watch time, and new/casual/regular viewer segmentation; TikTok exposes posting workflows and developer constraints through its Content Posting APIs and guidelines; LinkedIn exposes organic posting primitives and some company-level engagement data via its marketing APIs.
