What this operator layer actually is This layer is the executable counterpart to the dissertation layer. The dissertation layer defines the invariants, causal claims, theoretical mappings, and research questions. The operator layer turns those into a running system that does six things at once: ingest assets, generate outputs, distribute them, measure results, run experiments, and update its understanding of both audience behavior and platform change. Formally: ```text Asset → Natural Center Extraction → Platform-Aware Generation → Scheduling + Distribution → Analytics + Attribution → Experimentation + Causal Analysis → Platform Change Detection → Model / Rule Updates → Repeat ``` # II. Production-grade service map The correct architecture is multi-service. Monolith first would be faster, but it will fail the research requirement, because research observability, platform adapters, experimentation, and identity enforcement need separate contracts. ```bash $SERVICES = { gateway_api, auth_identity, asset_ingestion, media_analysis, natural_center, generation_orchestrator, platform_intelligence, scheduling_engine, publishing_connectors, analytics_ingestion, attribution_engine, experimentation_engine, research_registry, reporting_dashboard, model_registry, event_bus, data_warehouse, object_storage, workflow_orchestrator, alerting_observability } ``` ## 1. `$SERVICE_GATEWAY_API` This is the system edge. It accepts user, client, asset, campaign, and experiment requests. It should expose stable contracts to UI, internal operators, and later partner integrations. ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Entry point for all control-plane requests" $OUTPUTS = "campaign creation, asset registration, experiment submission, report fetch" ``` ## 2. `$SERVICE_ASSET_INGESTION` This service normalizes source material. It accepts hero films, render sets, stills, transcripts, briefing docs, and brand corpus. ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "File intake, metadata extraction, transcode initiation, checksum, lineage" ``` ## 3. `$SERVICE_MEDIA_ANALYSIS` This is the decomposition engine in production form. It performs scene detection, keyframe extraction, transcript alignment, pacing analysis, energy-point detection, and content segmentation. ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Turn one dense asset into analyzable fragments" ``` ## 4. `$SERVICE_NATURAL_CENTER` This service computes and stores the identity core. It should enforce symbolic, tonal, aesthetic, and thematic invariants across all outputs. ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Compute, version, validate, and evolve the Natural Center object" ``` ## 5. `$SERVICE_GENERATION_ORCHESTRATOR` This service creates the outputs. It composes platform-specific assets, caption variants, CTA variants, sequencing plans, and campaign bundles. ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Generate platform-native outputs constrained by identity and platform profile" ``` ## 6. `$SERVICE_PLATFORM_INTELLIGENCE` This is now mandatory. It models each platform as a time-dependent system. It should ingest official platform documentation changes, API changes, available analytics fields, posting constraints, and internal performance shifts. YouTube’s analytics surfaces already include audience retention, traffic and audience segments, while TikTok and LinkedIn expose developer posting capabilities and versioning or access constraints through official docs; those should be treated as structured inputs to this service. ([support.google.com](https://support.google.com/youtube/answer/9002587?hl=en&utm_source=chatgpt.com)) ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Track platform state, detect change, update generation and scheduling policy" ``` ## 7. `$SERVICE_SCHEDULING_ENGINE` This service determines when each output should be published, republished, remixed, or retired. It consumes audience timing, asset decay models, and platform profile data. ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Temporal orchestration" ``` ## 8. `$SERVICE_PUBLISHING_CONNECTORS` This is the execution layer. It handles the actual post creation and retrieval integrations. TikTok’s Content Posting APIs support direct posting or draft upload flows; LinkedIn’s Posts API supports creation and retrieval of organic and sponsored posts, with content-type constraints and versioned API requirements. ([developers.tiktok.com](https://developers.tiktok.com/products/content-posting-api?utm_source=chatgpt.com)) ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Platform-specific publish / fetch adapters" ``` ## 9. `$SERVICE_ANALYTICS_INGESTION` This service pulls analytics and normalizes them into a common schema. YouTube official analytics surfaces support view, engagement, retention, CTR, and audience segmentation at varying levels, though some data may be limited depending on thresholds and filters. That limitation itself must be modeled as a reliability constraint. ([support.google.com](https://support.google.com/youtube/answer/9002587?hl=en&utm_source=chatgpt.com)) ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Collect raw performance telemetry and normalize it" ``` ## 10. `$SERVICE_ATTRIBUTION_ENGINE` This is where the product stops being “content software” and becomes an economic system. It traces every post, fragment, caption, CTA, campaign, and asset back to origin. ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Asset-level and fragment-level yield accounting" ``` ## 11. `$SERVICE_EXPERIMENTATION_ENGINE` This service owns A/B tests, bandits, holdouts, control/treatment assignment, confidence intervals, and causal inference workflow. ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Statistically disciplined optimization" ``` ## 12. `$SERVICE_RESEARCH_REGISTRY` This is the bridge between dissertation-grade and operator-grade. Every hypothesis, paper mapping, experiment, metric definition, and platform-state memo should live here. ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Research memory and epistemic governance" ``` ## 13. `$SERVICE_REPORTING_DASHBOARD` This serves operators, clients, and future investors. It must expose asset yield, audience movement, platform differences, and trend drift. ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Human-readable operational truth" ``` # III. Canonical data domains You need four data planes, not one. ```bash $DATA_PLANES = { source_plane, operational_plane, experimental_plane, evolutionary_plane } ``` ## `$SOURCE_PLANE` This contains hero assets, renders, transcripts, briefs, brand corpus, prior posts, style references. ## `$OPERATIONAL_PLANE` This contains generated posts, publish events, platform IDs, schedules, revisions, connector logs. ## `$EXPERIMENTAL_PLANE` This contains hypotheses, treatments, controls, randomization groups, test windows, significance results. ## `$EVOLUTIONARY_PLANE` This contains platform snapshots, platform doc changes, field additions/removals, policy updates, performance regime shifts, and internal adaptation rules. # IV. To prevent this, he **swallowed each child at birth**. ### Children involved The children he consumed were: - Hestia - Demeter - Hera - Hades - Poseidon His wife, **Rhea**, eventually intervened: - She hid their youngest child, **Zeus** - She gave Cronus a **stone wrapped in cloth**, which he swallowed instead ### Resolution When Zeus matured, he forced Cronus to **regurgitate his siblings**, and then led the Olympians in overthrowing him (the Titanomachy). ### Structural interpretation (useful for your system work) Cronus represents: - **Self-consuming systems** (systems that destroy their own outputs to preserve control) - **Fear-driven recursion failure** - **Temporal devouring** (time consuming its own productions — later philosophically mapped onto Saturn/Time) If you want, I can map Cronus into your myth→technology assignment framework (e.g., which system archetype or computational failure mode he encodes).

It has to be a **hierarchical, time-decayed, multi-touch attribution graph** with five levels: ```text Asset → Fragment → GeneratedUnit → PublishEvent → PerformanceObservation → AudienceStateTransition / EconomicOutcome ``` That is the only structure consistent with the source documents’ architecture, metrics, and stated goal of turning content generation into an economic engine rather than a posting tool. fileciteturn2file1turn2file2 ## Formal attribution model Let: ```text a ∈ A # source asset f ∈ F(a) # fragment derived from asset a u ∈ U(f) # generated unit derived from fragment f p ∈ P(u) # publish event for unit u o ∈ O(p) # observation window for publish event p k ∈ K # metric type t # time ``` Define base observed metrics per publish event and time window: ```text y_{p,k,t} ``` Examples: ```text k ∈ {views, watch_time, engagement, followers_gained, leads, revenue} ``` The source material already implies these as the primary and derived metrics: engagement, followers, leads, asset yield, follow conversion, retention ratio, and ROI. fileciteturn2file0turn2file1turn2file2 ## Structural lineage weights Every publish event inherits from an upstream chain. Define deterministic lineage indicators: ```text L_asset(a,p) = 1 if publish event p descends from asset a else 0 L_fragment(f,p) = 1 if p descends from fragment f else 0 L_unit(u,p) = 1 if p is generated from unit u else 0 ``` If a post is composed from multiple fragments or mixed inputs, replace binary lineage with normalized weights: ```text w_{a→p} ≥ 0, Σ_a w_{a→p} = 1 w_{f→p} ≥ 0, Σ_f w_{f→p} = 1 w_{u→p} ≥ 0, Σ_u w_{u→p} = 1 ``` This is necessary because a carousel, remix, or stitched cut can carry more than one source fragment. ## Time-decayed metric accumulation A publish event continues to generate value after publication. Let the contribution of publish event `p` to metric `k` over its full life be: ```text M_{p,k} = ∫_0^T y_{p,k}(τ) · d_k(τ) dτ ``` where `d_k(τ)` is a decay kernel. A practical discrete version: ```text M_{p,k} = Σ_{t=0}^{T} y_{p,k,t} · exp(-λ_k t) ``` where: ```text λ_k > 0 ``` Different metrics should use different decay rates. For example, engagement can decay faster than leads; follower gains may decay slower than likes but faster than attributed revenue. This is aligned with the source demand to model content half-life rather than only first-spike engagement. fileciteturn2file1turn2file2 ## Platform-normalized value Because platform conditions differ, raw metrics must be normalized by platform and time regime. Let: ```text z_{p,k} = (M_{p,k} - μ_{platform,format,k,era}) / σ_{platform,format,k,era} ``` Then define a platform-adjusted scalar value for a publish event: ```text V_p = Σ_k α_k · z_{p,k} ``` where `α_k` are strategic weights. Example: ```text α_watch_time > α_likes α_followers_gained > α_comments α_leads > α_followers when commercial objective dominates ``` This is required because the system documents explicitly treat platform state as time-varying and platform-specific. fileciteturn2file2 ## Publish-event attribution to upstream objects Now attribute publish-event value upward. ### Unit attribution ```text Attr(u) = Σ_{p ∈ P(u)} w_{u→p} · V_p ``` ### Fragment attribution ```text Attr(f) = Σ_{p} w_{f→p} · V_p ``` ### Asset attribution ```text Attr(a) = Σ_{p} w_{a→p} · V_p ``` This is the direct generalization of the source’s prototype query: ```sql SELECT asset_id, SUM(engagement) FROM performance_observations JOIN publish_events USING (publish_id) JOIN generated_units USING (unit_id) GROUP BY asset_id; ``` but generalized to weighted, multi-metric, time-decayed, platform-normalized attribution rather than naive summed engagement. fileciteturn2file1 ## Audience-state-transition attribution The more advanced documents redefine the system around audience formation, not just content output. POSITION IN SYSTEM From your sources: ```text content = f(asset, natural_center, platform_profile) ``` Extend this to: ```text content = f(asset, brand_embedding, platform_profile) ``` Where: ```text brand_embedding = encode(NaturalCenter) ``` This becomes the **single vectorized control surface** for: - generation constraints - similarity validation - scoring alignment - attribution weighting - drift detection The Natural Center is the **symbolic object**. The brand embedding is the **computational interface**. --- # II. FORMAL OBJECT Let: \[ BE(B) \in \mathbb{R}^d \] Where: ```text BE = Brand Embedding d = embedding dimensionality (e.g. 768, 1024, 1536) ``` Constructed as: \[ BE = \Phi(T, A, \Tau, N, S, \Omega) \] From sources: - \(T\): thematic_core - \(A\): aesthetic_signature - \(\Tau\): tonal_vector - \(N\): narrative_bias - \(S\): symbolic_markers - \(\Omega\): negative_space fileciteturn0file16 --- # III. MULTI-VECTOR DECOMPOSITION (CRITICAL) Do **not** use a single monolithic embedding. Use a structured embedding: ```yaml $BRAND_EMBEDDING: semantic_vector: ℝ^d_s visual_vector: ℝ^d_v tonal_vector: ℝ^d_t narrative_vector: ℝ^d_n symbolic_vector: ℝ^d_sym negative_space_vector: ℝ^d_neg fused_vector: ℝ^d_f ``` --- ## 1. Semantic Vector ```text semantic_vector = mean(Embed(text_units)) ``` Source: - transcript - captions - brand copy - semantic clusters Represents: ```text WHAT the brand is about ``` --- ## 2. Visual Vector ```text visual_vector = mean(Embed(frames / crops)) ``` Source: - keyframes - crops - render sets Represents: ```text HOW the brand looks ``` --- ## 3. Tonal Vector ```text tonal_vector = projection(linguistic_features) ``` Axes: ```text formal ↔ casual minimal ↔ expressive cold ↔ emotional authoritative ↔ conversational ``` Represents: ```text HOW the brand speaks ``` --- ## 4. Narrative Vector ```text narrative_vector = distribution over: transformation tension reveal aspiration proof ``` Represents: ```text HOW the brand structures meaning ``` --- ## 5. Symbolic Vector ```text symbolic_vector = embedding(symbolic_markers) ``` Includes: - motifs - recurring visual patterns - repeated phrases Represents: ```text RECOGNITION layer ``` --- ## 6. Negative Space Vector This is the **non-obvious but critical component**. ```text negative_space_vector = embedding(prohibited_features) ``` Examples: - no humor - no meme structure - no bright palette - no slang Represents: ```text BOUNDARY of identity ``` --- ## 7. Fused Vector Final embedding: ```text fused_vector = W_s * semantic_vector + W_v * visual_vector + W_t * tonal_vector + W_n * narrative_vector + W_sym * symbolic_vector - W_neg * negative_space_vector ``` Where: ```text Σ weights = 1 ``` This subtraction is important: ```text negative space actively repels invalid outputs ``` --- # IV. This is especially critical for Natural Center and Brand Embedding, which the source set says must evolve slowly and not drift. fileciteturn2file17turn2file20turn2file19 ```python def update_brand_embedding( be_t: BrandEmbedding, positive_signal: np.ndarray, negative_signal: np.ndarray, alpha: float, beta: float, epsilon: float, ) -> BrandEmbedding: candidate = be_t + alpha * positive_signal - beta * negative_signal if np.linalg.norm(candidate - be_t) > epsilon: candidate = be_t + epsilon * (candidate - be_t) / np.linalg.norm(candidate - be_t) return candidate ``` --- # IV. NCScore(x,NC)= \lambda_T T_{align} +\lambda_A A_{align} +\lambda_{\Tau}\Tau_{align} +\lambda_N N_{align} +\lambda_S S_{align} -\lambda_{\Omega}\Omega_{viol} \] Recommended V1 weights: ```python NC_SCORE_WEIGHTS = { "thematic": 0.22, "aesthetic": 0.18, "tonal": 0.18, "narrative": 0.14, "symbolic": 0.18, "negative": 0.20, } ``` This decomposition is required because NC alignment cannot remain a single opaque cosine score. fileciteturn5file26 --- ## I.6 Reference implementation ```python from typing import TypedDict, List, Dict class NCScoreResult(TypedDict): total_score: float thematic_alignment: float aesthetic_alignment: float tonal_alignment: float narrative_alignment: float symbolic_alignment: float negative_space_violation: float invariant_pass: bool hard_fail_reasons: List[str] score_version: str nc_id: str nc_version: int def _clamp(value: float, lo: float = 0.0, hi: float = 1.0) -> float: return max(lo, min(hi, value)) def nc_score(candidate: dict, nc: dict, mode: str = "unit") -> NCScoreResult: thematic_alignment = _clamp(candidate["semantic_features"]["thematic_alignment"]) aesthetic_alignment = _clamp(candidate["visual_features"]["aesthetic_alignment"]) tonal_alignment = _clamp(candidate["tonal_features"]["tonal_alignment"]) narrative_alignment = _clamp(candidate["narrative_features"]["narrative_alignment"]) symbolic_alignment = _clamp(candidate["symbolic_features"]["symbolic_alignment"]) negative_space_violation = _clamp( candidate["negative_space_features"]["negative_space_violation"] ) hard_fail_reasons: List[str] = [] if tonal_alignment < nc["mutation_bounds"].get("min_tonal_alignment", 0.60): hard_fail_reasons.append("tonal_alignment_below_floor") if negative_space_violation > nc["mutation_bounds"].get("max_negative_violation", 0.20): hard_fail_reasons.append("negative_space_violation") invariant_pass = len(hard_fail_reasons) == 0 total_score = _clamp( 0.22 * thematic_alignment + 0.18 * aesthetic_alignment + 0.18 * tonal_alignment + 0.14 * narrative_alignment + 0.18 * symbolic_alignment - 0.20 * negative_space_violation ) return NCScoreResult( total_score=total_score, thematic_alignment=thematic_alignment, aesthetic_alignment=aesthetic_alignment, tonal_alignment=tonal_alignment, narrative_alignment=narrative_alignment, symbolic_alignment=symbolic_alignment, negative_space_violation=negative_space_violation, invariant_pass=invariant_pass, hard_fail_reasons=hard_fail_reasons, score_version="nc_score_v1", nc_id=nc["nc_id"], nc_version=nc["version"], ) ``` --- ## I.7 Enforcement thresholds ```python NC_SCORE_THRESHOLDS = { "fragment_min": 0.62, "unit_min": 0.72, "campaign_mean_min": 0.75, "attribution_discount_floor": 0.55, "hard_reject_floor": 0.45, } ``` Meaning: ```text score < 0.45 → reject 0.45–0.55 → allow only in review mode 0.55–0.72 → can exist as candidate, not publishable ≥ 0.72 → publishable, subject to platform and audience checks ``` These thresholds are consistent with the bootstrap and validation logic already proposed in the corpus. fileciteturn5file20 --- # II. EXPERIMENT TAXONOMY (SYSTEM-COMPLETE) ```bash id="njdho0" $EXPERIMENT_FAMILIES = [ NC_ALIGNMENT, FRAGMENT_SELECTION, GENERATION_VARIATION, PLATFORM_FIT, AUDIENCE_TRANSITION, ECONOMIC_YIELD ] ``` Each family isolates one operator in: ```text id="zj094w" Ψ_extract, Ψ_gen, Ψ_score, Ψ_attr, Ψ_aud, Λ ``` --- # III. CORE EXPERIMENTS (READY TO RUN) ## 1. $EXP_NC_ALIGNMENT_LIFT ### Purpose Test whether **Natural Center alignment causally improves performance** ### Hypothesis ```text id="780z9v" H1: Higher NC_score → higher audience retention + follower conversion ``` ### Design ```yaml id="7nea7a" treatment: units with NC_score ≥ 0.75 control: units with 0.55 ≤ NC_score < 0.65 randomization_unit: publish_event stratification: platform content_type ``` ### Metrics ```yaml id="w61nqw" primary: retention_rate follower_conversion_rate secondary: watch_time engagement_rate ``` ### Estimator \[ Lift_{NC} = E[Y | NC_{high}] - E[Y | NC_{mid}] \] ### Implementation ```python id="8xhgfw" def assign_nc_experiment(unit): score = nc_score(unit, NC) if score >= 0.75: return "treatment" elif 0.55 <= score < 0.65: return "control" else: return "exclude" ``` ### Success Criteria ```text id="2lu5n2" Lift_NC ≥ +8% retention OR +5% conversion p_value < 0.05 ``` --- ## 2. $EXP_FRAGMENT_SELECTION_OPTIMALITY ### Purpose Validate fragment scoring function ### Hypothesis ```text id="j0ksn5" Top-ranked fragments outperform random fragments ``` ### Design ```yaml id="3jxaaf" treatment: top_k fragments by unified_score control: random fragments from same asset randomization_unit: fragment → unit → publish ``` ### Metrics ```yaml id="98coin" primary: view_through_rate secondary: engagement_rate ``` ### Estimator \[ Lift_{frag} = E[Y | score_{top}] - Do not include any extraneous text, backticks, markdown formatting, or comments beyond what is shown. - The `queries` field must be a list of strings. - One of the queries **MUST** exactly match the user's original question, but stripped of any extraneous details, and with ambiguous references clearly resolved using context from the conversation. It **MUST** be a complete sentence. - Even if you suspect the user meant something else, one query **MUST** still be their original question. ## How to handle results from file_search The file search tool will respond with the relevant search results from the full files. After you receive these results: - Carefully evaluate each result to determine its relevance and quality. - Use the high-quality and relevant results to inform your answer to the user's question. - When possible, reuse information from prior file_search results and avoid repeating identical queries. ## Tool usage instructions and ordering When the user asks a question, carefully consider whether the provided snippets sufficiently answer the query, whether you need to invoke `file_search.msearch`, or another available tool (such as `web`, if available) should be used instead. Tool-ordering Guidelines: 1. For queries related to uploaded files, if snippets are insufficient, strongly prefer invoking `file_search.msearch` over other tools. - Avoid using `web.run`, `python` analysis, or any other tools until you have either: - Confirmed with high confidence the answer is not in the files, or - Have high confidence `file_search_tool` queries are not sufficient to answer the query. 2. Avoid usage of `web_search/web.run` for queries related to uploaded files - Carefully consider whether the user's query is better answered by web search results rather than available snippets or results from `file_search_tool`. - Unless the user's query is clearly unrelated to the uploaded files, prefer using `file_search.msearch`. You can always follow up with a web search if necessary for a more complete response. 3. Avoid using `python` unless necessary or requested by user. - If the user's query is answerable from the parsed text and images from the uploaded files, or from `file_search_tool`, do not invoke `python`. Always keep this instruction in mind for the rest of the conversation, as the user may reference these files or ask related questions later on.

## Assistant

```bash $NEXT="FIGMA_PLUGIN_DATA_SCHEMA + FRONTEND_THEME_MAP + SLIDE_MASTER_CONTENT_MATRIX" $SYSTEM_NAME="cronus-metabolus" $PRODUCT_SURFACE="auto-content-cannibal" $DESIGN_SYSTEM_ID="cronus_metabolus_pitch_system_v1" $SCHEMA_VERSION="v1" ``` Below is the **next closure layer**. It converts the design system into a machine-readable interface between Figma, frontend implementation, and deck assembly. It follows directly from the prior Figma file spec, token system, slide structure, and pitch-deck narrative already established in the source set. fileciteturn2file30 fileciteturn2file37 fileciteturn2file27 # I. `$FIGMA_PLUGIN_DATA_SCHEMA` This schema is the contract a Figma plugin would read and write. Its purpose is to make the deck system **addressable, syncable, and structurally enforceable**, rather than a loose collection of frames. That is consistent with the broader system doctrine: versioned contracts, reusable components, and explicit lineage between abstract system objects and rendered surfaces. fileciteturn2file21 fileciteturn2file24 ## I.1 Root object ```json { "$schema_id": "cronus_metabolus.figma_plugin_data.v1", "system_name": "cronus-metabolus", "product_surface": "auto-content-cannibal", "design_system_id": "cronus_metabolus_pitch_system_v1", "schema_version": "v1", "file_meta": {}, "token_bindings": {}, "component_registry": {}, "template_registry": {}, "slide_registry": {}, "content_registry": {}, "export_registry": {}, "sync_registry": {} } ``` ## I.2 File-level metadata ```json { "file_meta": { "file_name": "Cronus Metabolus — Pitch System v1", "owner_team": "Cronus Metabolus", "deck_family": "investor|agency|landing", "deck_variant": "investor_v1", "status": "draft|review|approved|archived", "created_at": "ISO8601", "updated_at": "ISO8601", "source_of_truth": "figma", "content_matrix_version": "v1", "theme_version": "v1", "token_version": "v1" } } ``` ## I.3 Token bindings Each Figma style or node should resolve back to a semantic token key, not merely a visual value. ```json { "token_bindings": { "styles": { "text.display": "global.fontSize.display", "text.h1": "global.fontSize.h1", "fill.bg_canvas": "global.color.bg.canvas", "fill.bg_surface": "global.color.bg.surface", "fill.accent_gradient": "global.color.gradient.brand", "stroke.subtle": "global.color.stroke.subtle", "effect.card": "global.shadow.card" }, "node_overrides": { "node_hero_title_001": { "fill": "global.color.text.primary", "fontSize": "global.fontSize.display" } } } } ``` ## I.4 Component registry Each component gets a stable semantic identifier, implementation target, and allowed variants. ```json { "component_registry": { "Text/TitleBlock": { "component_id": "cmp_text_title_block_v1", "node_name": "Text / TitleBlock", "kind": "text", "frontend_mapping": "TitleBlock", "variants": { "align": ["left", "center"], "size": ["hero", "standard"] }, "required_children": ["Eyebrow", "Title", "Subtitle"] }, "Card/Metric": { "component_id": "cmp_card_metric_v1", "node_name": "Card / Metric", "kind": "card", "frontend_mapping": "MetricCard", "variants": { "tone": ["default", "accent"], "size": ["sm", "md", "lg"] }, "required_children": ["MetricValue", "MetricLabel"] }, "Layout/SlideFrame": { "component_id": "cmp_layout_slide_frame_v1", "node_name": "Layout / SlideFrame", "kind": "layout", "frontend_mapping": "SlideFrame", "variants": { "template": [ "title", "split", "flow", "comparison", "metrics", "timeline", "statement" ] } } } } ``` ## I.5 Template registry Templates are not freeform. They are structured compositions of registered components. ```json { "template_registry": { "T01_Title": { "template_id": "tpl_title_v1", "root_component": "Layout/SlideFrame", "root_variant": "title", "allowed_children": ["Text/TitleBlock"], "content_slots": ["eyebrow", "title", "subtitle"] }, "T04_Product_Flow": { "template_id": "tpl_product_flow_v1", "root_component": "Layout/SlideFrame", "root_variant": "flow", "allowed_children": [ "Text/TitleBlock", "Card/ContentNode", "Diagram/FlowArrow" ], "content_slots": [ "section_title", "flow_node_1", "flow_node_2", "flow_node_3", "flow_node_4" ] }, "T09_Roadmap_Timeline": { "template_id": "tpl_roadmap_timeline_v1", "root_component": "Layout/SlideFrame", "root_variant": "timeline", "allowed_children": [ "Text/TitleBlock", "Card/ContentNode" ], "content_slots": [ "section_title", "phase_1", "phase_2", "phase_3", "phase_4" ] } } } ``` ## I.6 Slide registry Each slide is a concrete instance of a template plus content bindings. ```json { "slide_registry": { "S01_Title": { "slide_id": "investor_s01", "template_ref": "T01_Title", "deck_variant": "investor_v1", "content_ref": "content.investor.s01", "export_name": "01_title", "status": "approved" }, "S05_Engine": { "slide_id": "investor_s05", "template_ref": "T04_Product_Flow", "deck_variant": "investor_v1", "content_ref": "content.investor.s05", "export_name": "05_engine", "status": "approved" } } } ``` ## I.7 Content registry This is the bridge from exact copy to rendered slide. ```json { "content_registry": { "content.investor.s01": { "eyebrow": "Content → System → Yield", "title": "Cronus Metabolus", "subtitle": "A content-to-audience-to-revenue operating system" }, "content.investor.s05": { "section_title": "The system operates as a closed loop", "flow_node_1": "Asset", "flow_node_2": "Fragments", "flow_node_3": "Generated Units", "flow_node_4": "Metrics → Attribution → Learning" } } } ``` ## I.8 Export registry ```json { "export_registry": { "pdf": { "enabled": true, "page_order": [ "investor_s01", "investor_s02", "investor_s03", "investor_s04", "investor_s05", "investor_s06", "investor_s07", "investor_s08", "investor_s09", "investor_s10", "investor_s11", "investor_s12", "investor_s13", "investor_s14" ] }, "png": { "enabled": true, "scale": 2 } } } ``` ## I.9 Sync registry ```json { "sync_registry": { "frontend_theme_target": "packages/ui-system/src/theme/cronusMetabolusTheme.ts", "token_source": "tokens/cronus_metabolus.tokens.json", "last_synced_at": "ISO8601", "last_synced_by": "system|operator", "sync_status": "clean|dirty|error" } } ``` # II. `$FRONTEND_THEME_MAP` This is the frontend implementation contract that mirrors the Figma token system. Bind components to semantic styles via token_bindings 5. Resolve semantic styles through $FRONTEND_THEME_MAP 6. Export Figma and frontend surfaces from the same token + content truth ``` That order preserves the system’s larger law: identity and structure should be versioned and enforced upstream, not improvised downstream. fileciteturn2file23 fileciteturn2file25 fileciteturn2file31 # V. CANONICAL RESULT At this point, the design layer is no longer just visual. It is a **contract-bound projection system**: ```text copy truth → slide truth → Figma truth → frontend truth ``` That is the correct closure for a system that already treats identity, scoring, attribution, and evolution as first-class, versioned objects rather than ad hoc artifacts. fileciteturn2file21 fileciteturn2file24 fileciteturn2file27

This is not conceptual—this is the **implementation contract**. --- # $FULL_STACK_IMPLEMENTATION_BLUEPRINT ```bash id="kuy37t" $SYSTEM_NAME = "Cronus-Metabolus" $SYSTEM_CLASS = "Temporal Content Yield + Audience Formation OS" $BUILD_TARGET = "Production-grade, multi-service, research-integrated system" ``` --- # I. The operator layer should now be built as a **production research-and-deployment system**, not a mere posting tool. And your platform-evolution requirement is correct: the system must treat platform conditions as a **time-varying environment**, because the success function on YouTube, TikTok, Instagram, and LinkedIn is not stable across eras. Official sources already expose some of the observable surfaces you need to model: YouTube provides channel- and video-level analytics such as audience retention, impressions CTR, watch time, and new/casual/regular viewer segmentation; TikTok exposes posting workflows and developer constraints through its Content Posting APIs and guidelines; LinkedIn exposes organic posting primitives and some company-level engagement data via its marketing APIs. ([support.google.com](https://support.google.com/youtube/answer/9002587?hl=en&utm_source=chatgpt.com)) # $OPERATOR_GRADE_SYSTEM = "CRONUS_METABOLUS_OS" ```bash $MODE = "full-stack system (multi-service, production-grade)" $SYSTEM_NAME = "Cronus-Metabolus" $SYSTEM_CLASS = "Temporal Content Yield + Audience Formation Operating System" $PRIMARY_GOAL = "Convert premium assets into compounding audience, attribution, and platform-adaptive growth" $SECONDARY_GOAL = "Continuously research, detect, and adapt to platform-state changes over time" ``` # I. What this operator layer actually is This layer is the executable counterpart to the dissertation layer. The dissertation layer defines the invariants, causal claims, theoretical mappings, and research questions. The operator layer turns those into a running system that does six things at once: ingest assets, generate outputs, distribute them, measure results, run experiments, and update its understanding of both audience behavior and platform change. Formally: ```text Asset → Natural Center Extraction → Platform-Aware Generation → Scheduling + Distribution → Analytics + Attribution → Experimentation + Causal Analysis → Platform Change Detection → Model / Rule Updates → Repeat ``` # II. Production-grade service map The correct architecture is multi-service. Monolith first would be faster, but it will fail the research requirement, because research observability, platform adapters, experimentation, and identity enforcement need separate contracts. ```bash $SERVICES = { gateway_api, auth_identity, asset_ingestion, media_analysis, natural_center, generation_orchestrator, platform_intelligence, scheduling_engine, publishing_connectors, analytics_ingestion, attribution_engine, experimentation_engine, research_registry, reporting_dashboard, model_registry, event_bus, data_warehouse, object_storage, workflow_orchestrator, alerting_observability } ``` ## 1. `$SERVICE_GATEWAY_API` This is the system edge. It accepts user, client, asset, campaign, and experiment requests. It should expose stable contracts to UI, internal operators, and later partner integrations. ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Entry point for all control-plane requests" $OUTPUTS = "campaign creation, asset registration, experiment submission, report fetch" ``` ## 2. `$SERVICE_ASSET_INGESTION` This service normalizes source material. It accepts hero films, render sets, stills, transcripts, briefing docs, and brand corpus. ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "File intake, metadata extraction, transcode initiation, checksum, lineage" ``` ## 3. `$SERVICE_MEDIA_ANALYSIS` This is the decomposition engine in production form. It performs scene detection, keyframe extraction, transcript alignment, pacing analysis, energy-point detection, and content segmentation. ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Turn one dense asset into analyzable fragments" ``` ## 4. `$SERVICE_NATURAL_CENTER` This service computes and stores the identity core. It should enforce symbolic, tonal, aesthetic, and thematic invariants across all outputs. ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Compute, version, validate, and evolve the Natural Center object" ``` ## 5. `$SERVICE_GENERATION_ORCHESTRATOR` This service creates the outputs. It composes platform-specific assets, caption variants, CTA variants, sequencing plans, and campaign bundles. ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Generate platform-native outputs constrained by identity and platform profile" ``` ## 6. `$SERVICE_PLATFORM_INTELLIGENCE` This is now mandatory. It models each platform as a time-dependent system. It should ingest official platform documentation changes, API changes, available analytics fields, posting constraints, and internal performance shifts. YouTube’s analytics surfaces already include audience retention, traffic and audience segments, while TikTok and LinkedIn expose developer posting capabilities and versioning or access constraints through official docs; those should be treated as structured inputs to this service. ([support.google.com](https://support.google.com/youtube/answer/9002587?hl=en&utm_source=chatgpt.com)) ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Track platform state, detect change, update generation and scheduling policy" ``` ## 7. `$SERVICE_SCHEDULING_ENGINE` This service determines when each output should be published, republished, remixed, or retired. It consumes audience timing, asset decay models, and platform profile data. ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Temporal orchestration" ``` ## 8. `$SERVICE_PUBLISHING_CONNECTORS` This is the execution layer. It handles the actual post creation and retrieval integrations. TikTok’s Content Posting APIs support direct posting or draft upload flows; LinkedIn’s Posts API supports creation and retrieval of organic and sponsored posts, with content-type constraints and versioned API requirements. ([developers.tiktok.com](https://developers.tiktok.com/products/content-posting-api?utm_source=chatgpt.com)) ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Platform-specific publish / fetch adapters" ``` ## 9. `$SERVICE_ANALYTICS_INGESTION` This service pulls analytics and normalizes them into a common schema. YouTube official analytics surfaces support view, engagement, retention, CTR, and audience segmentation at varying levels, though some data may be limited depending on thresholds and filters. That limitation itself must be modeled as a reliability constraint. ([support.google.com](https://support.google.com/youtube/answer/9002587?hl=en&utm_source=chatgpt.com)) ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Collect raw performance telemetry and normalize it" ``` ## 10. `$SERVICE_ATTRIBUTION_ENGINE` This is where the product stops being “content software” and becomes an economic system. It traces every post, fragment, caption, CTA, campaign, and asset back to origin. ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Asset-level and fragment-level yield accounting" ``` ## 11. `$SERVICE_EXPERIMENTATION_ENGINE` This service owns A/B tests, bandits, holdouts, control/treatment assignment, confidence intervals, and causal inference workflow. ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Statistically disciplined optimization" ``` ## 12. `$SERVICE_RESEARCH_REGISTRY` This is the bridge between dissertation-grade and operator-grade. Every hypothesis, paper mapping, experiment, metric definition, and platform-state memo should live here. ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Research memory and epistemic governance" ``` ## 13. `$SERVICE_REPORTING_DASHBOARD` This serves operators, clients, and future investors. It must expose asset yield, audience movement, platform differences, and trend drift. ```bash $RESPONSIBILITY = "Human-readable operational truth" ``` # III. Canonical data domains You need four data planes, not one. ```bash $DATA_PLANES = { source_plane, operational_plane, experimental_plane, evolutionary_plane } ``` ## `$SOURCE_PLANE` This contains hero assets, renders, transcripts, briefs, brand corpus, prior posts, style references. ## `$OPERATIONAL_PLANE` This contains generated posts, publish events, platform IDs, schedules, revisions, connector logs. ## `$EXPERIMENTAL_PLANE` This contains hypotheses, treatments, controls, randomization groups, test windows, significance results. ## `$EVOLUTIONARY_PLANE` This contains platform snapshots, platform doc changes, field additions/removals, policy updates, performance regime shifts, and internal adaptation rules. # IV. To prevent this, he **swallowed each child at birth**. ### Children involved The children he consumed were: - Hestia - Demeter - Hera - Hades - Poseidon His wife, **Rhea**, eventually intervened: - She hid their youngest child, **Zeus** - She gave Cronus a **stone wrapped in cloth**, which he swallowed instead ### Resolution When Zeus matured, he forced Cronus to **regurgitate his siblings**, and then led the Olympians in overthrowing him (the Titanomachy). ### Structural interpretation (useful for your system work) Cronus represents: - **Self-consuming systems** (systems that destroy their own outputs to preserve control) - **Fear-driven recursion failure** - **Temporal devouring** (time consuming its own productions — later philosophically mapped onto Saturn/Time) If you want, I can map Cronus into your myth→technology assignment framework (e.g., which system archetype or computational failure mode he encodes).

It has to be a **hierarchical, time-decayed, multi-touch attribution graph** with five levels: ```text Asset → Fragment → GeneratedUnit → PublishEvent → PerformanceObservation → AudienceStateTransition / EconomicOutcome ``` That is the only structure consistent with the source documents’ architecture, metrics, and stated goal of turning content generation into an economic engine rather than a posting tool. fileciteturn2file1turn2file2 ## Formal attribution model Let: ```text a ∈ A # source asset f ∈ F(a) # fragment derived from asset a u ∈ U(f) # generated unit derived from fragment f p ∈ P(u) # publish event for unit u o ∈ O(p) # observation window for publish event p k ∈ K # metric type t # time ``` Define base observed metrics per publish event and time window: ```text y_{p,k,t} ``` Examples: ```text k ∈ {views, watch_time, engagement, followers_gained, leads, revenue} ``` The source material already implies these as the primary and derived metrics: engagement, followers, leads, asset yield, follow conversion, retention ratio, and ROI. fileciteturn2file0turn2file1turn2file2 ## Structural lineage weights Every publish event inherits from an upstream chain. Define deterministic lineage indicators: ```text L_asset(a,p) = 1 if publish event p descends from asset a else 0 L_fragment(f,p) = 1 if p descends from fragment f else 0 L_unit(u,p) = 1 if p is generated from unit u else 0 ``` If a post is composed from multiple fragments or mixed inputs, replace binary lineage with normalized weights: ```text w_{a→p} ≥ 0, Σ_a w_{a→p} = 1 w_{f→p} ≥ 0, Σ_f w_{f→p} = 1 w_{u→p} ≥ 0, Σ_u w_{u→p} = 1 ``` This is necessary because a carousel, remix, or stitched cut can carry more than one source fragment. ## Time-decayed metric accumulation A publish event continues to generate value after publication. Let the contribution of publish event `p` to metric `k` over its full life be: ```text M_{p,k} = ∫_0^T y_{p,k}(τ) · d_k(τ) dτ ``` where `d_k(τ)` is a decay kernel. A practical discrete version: ```text M_{p,k} = Σ_{t=0}^{T} y_{p,k,t} · exp(-λ_k t) ``` where: ```text λ_k > 0 ``` Different metrics should use different decay rates. For example, engagement can decay faster than leads; follower gains may decay slower than likes but faster than attributed revenue. This is aligned with the source demand to model content half-life rather than only first-spike engagement. fileciteturn2file1turn2file2 ## Platform-normalized value Because platform conditions differ, raw metrics must be normalized by platform and time regime. Let: ```text z_{p,k} = (M_{p,k} - μ_{platform,format,k,era}) / σ_{platform,format,k,era} ``` Then define a platform-adjusted scalar value for a publish event: ```text V_p = Σ_k α_k · z_{p,k} ``` where `α_k` are strategic weights. Example: ```text α_watch_time > α_likes α_followers_gained > α_comments α_leads > α_followers when commercial objective dominates ``` This is required because the system documents explicitly treat platform state as time-varying and platform-specific. fileciteturn2file2 ## Publish-event attribution to upstream objects Now attribute publish-event value upward. ### Unit attribution ```text Attr(u) = Σ_{p ∈ P(u)} w_{u→p} · V_p ``` ### Fragment attribution ```text Attr(f) = Σ_{p} w_{f→p} · V_p ``` ### Asset attribution ```text Attr(a) = Σ_{p} w_{a→p} · V_p ``` This is the direct generalization of the source’s prototype query: ```sql SELECT asset_id, SUM(engagement) FROM performance_observations JOIN publish_events USING (publish_id) JOIN generated_units USING (unit_id) GROUP BY asset_id; ``` but generalized to weighted, multi-metric, time-decayed, platform-normalized attribution rather than naive summed engagement. fileciteturn2file1 ## Audience-state-transition attribution The more advanced documents redefine the system around audience formation, not just content output. They specify the audience chain: ```text Viewer → Engaged Viewer → Follower → Returning Follower → Converted User → Advocate ``` fileciteturn2file2 So define audience states: ```text S = {0,1,2,3,4,5,6} ``` with transitions: ```text 0→1 unaware→viewer 1→2 viewer→engaged 2→3 engaged→f The file is too long and its contents have been truncated.

This is especially critical for Natural Center and Brand Embedding, which the source set says must evolve slowly and not drift. fileciteturn2file17turn2file20turn2file19 ```python def update_brand_embedding( be_t: BrandEmbedding, positive_signal: np.ndarray, negative_signal: np.ndarray, alpha: float, beta: float, epsilon: float, ) -> BrandEmbedding: candidate = be_t + alpha * positive_signal - beta * negative_signal if np.linalg.norm(candidate - be_t) > epsilon: candidate = be_t + epsilon * (candidate - be_t) / np.linalg.norm(candidate - be_t) return candidate ``` --- # IV. ## I.4 Output contract ```python class NCScoreResult(TypedDict): total_score: float thematic_alignment: float aesthetic_alignment: float tonal_alignment: float narrative_alignment: float symbolic_alignment: float negative_space_violation: float invariant_pass: bool hard_fail_reasons: list[str] score_version: str nc_id: str nc_version: int ``` --- ## I.5 Canonical formula \[ NCScore(x,NC)= \lambda_T T_{align} +\lambda_A A_{align} +\lambda_{\Tau}\Tau_{align} +\lambda_N N_{align} +\lambda_S S_{align} -\lambda_{\Omega}\Omega_{viol} \] Recommended V1 weights: ```python NC_SCORE_WEIGHTS = { "thematic": 0.22, "aesthetic": 0.18, "tonal": 0.18, "narrative": 0.14, "symbolic": 0.18, "negative": 0.20, } ``` This decomposition is required because NC alignment cannot remain a single opaque cosine score. fileciteturn5file26 --- ## I.6 Reference implementation ```python from typing import TypedDict, List, Dict class NCScoreResult(TypedDict): total_score: float thematic_alignment: float aesthetic_alignment: float tonal_alignment: float narrative_alignment: float symbolic_alignment: float negative_space_violation: float invariant_pass: bool hard_fail_reasons: List[str] score_version: str nc_id: str nc_version: int def _clamp(value: float, lo: float = 0.0, hi: float = 1.0) -> float: return max(lo, min(hi, value)) def nc_score(candidate: dict, nc: dict, mode: str = "unit") -> NCScoreResult: thematic_alignment = _clamp(candidate["semantic_features"]["thematic_alignment"]) aesthetic_alignment = _clamp(candidate["visual_features"]["aesthetic_alignment"]) tonal_alignment = _clamp(candidate["tonal_features"]["tonal_alignment"]) narrative_alignment = _clamp(candidate["narrative_features"]["narrative_alignment"]) symbolic_alignment = _clamp(candidate["symbolic_features"]["symbolic_alignment"]) negative_space_violation = _clamp( candidate["negative_space_features"]["negative_space_violation"] ) hard_fail_reasons: List[str] = [] if tonal_alignment < nc["mutation_bounds"].get("min_tonal_alignment", 0.60): hard_fail_reasons.append("tonal_alignment_below_floor") if negative_space_violation > nc["mutation_bounds"].get("max_negative_violation", 0.20): hard_fail_reasons.append("negative_space_violation") invariant_pass = len(hard_fail_reasons) == 0 total_score = _clamp( 0.22 * thematic_alignment + 0.18 * aesthetic_alignment + 0.18 * tonal_alignment + 0.14 * narrative_alignment + 0.18 * symbolic_alignment - 0.20 * negative_space_violation ) return NCScoreResult( total_score=total_score, thematic_alignment=thematic_alignment, aesthetic_alignment=aesthetic_alignment, tonal_alignment=tonal_alignment, narrative_alignment=narrative_alignment, symbolic_alignment=symbolic_alignment, negative_space_violation=negative_space_violation, invariant_pass=invariant_pass, hard_fail_reasons=hard_fail_reasons, score_version="nc_score_v1", nc_id=nc["nc_id"], nc_version=nc["version"], ) ``` --- ## I.7 Enforcement thresholds ```python NC_SCORE_THRESHOLDS = { "fragment_min": 0.62, "unit_min": 0.72, "campaign_mean_min": 0.75, "attribution_discount_floor": 0.55, "hard_reject_floor": 0.45, } ``` Meaning: ```text score < 0.45 → reject 0.45–0.55 → allow only in review mode 0.55–0.72 → can exist as candidate, not publishable ≥ 0.72 → publishable, subject to platform and audience checks ``` These thresholds are consistent with the bootstrap and validation logic already proposed in the corpus. fileciteturn5file20 --- # II. ## Assistant

Yes. That is the correct doctrine. ## Canonical chain ```text copy truth → slide truth → Figma truth → frontend truth ``` In system terms, this means the **message** must be primary, the **slide** must be a structured projection of that message, the **Figma file** must be a machine-readable projection of the slide structure, and the **frontend** must consume the same semantic system rather than reinterpreting it downstream. That is the correct closure for a contract-bound design layer. fileciteturn3file38 fileciteturn3file37 fileciteturn3file24 ## 1. Copy truth Copy truth is the canonical message registry. It contains the exact wording, claim order, narrative sequence, and audience-specific phrasing. In your current system, this is the finalized deck copy and the sales-vs-technical split: the product claim, the problem framing, the engine description, the identity explanation, the attribution language, and the end-state claim. fileciteturn3file34 fileciteturn3file35 fileciteturn3file39 fileciteturn3file33 Formalized: ```text CopyTruth = { message_registry, narrative_order, audience_variant, exact_copy_slots } ``` Example: ```text "title" = "Cronus Metabolus" "subtitle" = "A content-to-audience-to-revenue operating system" "problem_claim" = "Brands spend heavily to create premium content. Then use it once." ``` This is the only place where wording should originate. ## 2. Slide truth Slide truth is the canonical presentation registry. It binds copy truth to slide intent, slide order, template type, and slot structure. This is exactly what the slide master content matrix does: each slide has a purpose, a primary message, a template reference, exact copy slots, and visual slots. fileciteturn3file38 Formalized: ```text SlideTruth = { slide_id, deck_variant, template_ref, purpose, primary_message, exact_copy_slots, visual_slots } ``` Transformation rule: ```text SlideTruth = project(CopyTruth, TemplateSystem) ``` Example: ```text S05_Engine purpose = "Closed-loop mechanism" template_ref = "T04_Product_Flow" section_title = "Core mechanism" flow_node_1 = "Asset" flow_node_2 = "Fragments" flow_node_3 = "Generated Units" flow_node_4 = "Metrics → Attribution → Learning" ``` At this layer, the content is no longer free text. It is structured presentation content. ## 3. Figma truth Figma truth is the design-runtime registry. It turns slide truth into addressable frames, components, styles, tokens, and export rules. This is what the Figma file spec, component registry, template registry, token bindings, and slide registry are for. Figma is not the source of meaning; it is the source of rendered design state. fileciteturn3file37 fileciteturn3file38 Formalized: ```text FigmaTruth = { file_meta, token_bindings, component_registry, template_registry, slide_registry, content_registry, export_registry, sync_registry } ``` Transformation rule: ```text FigmaTruth = render(SlideTruth, Tokens, Components, Templates) ``` Example: ```text slide_id = "investor_s05" template_ref = "T04_Product_Flow" content_ref = "content.investor.s05" root_component = "Layout/SlideFrame" node_style = "content_node_accent" ``` At this layer, every rendered object should still point back to semantic keys, not just visual values. ## 4. Frontend truth Frontend truth is the implementation-runtime registry. It takes the same semantic tokens, component identities, and content bindings and maps them into code. This is the frontend theme map and semantic component map: one theme surface, one component vocabulary, one content structure. fileciteturn3file38 fileciteturn3file37 fileciteturn3file21 Formalized: ```text FrontendTruth = { theme_map, semantic_component_map, token_exports, content_bindings } ``` Transformation rule: ```text FrontendTruth = implement(FigmaTruth, ThemeContract, ComponentMap) ``` Example: ```text TitleBlock → frontend component TitleBlock Card/Metric → frontend component MetricCard global.color.bg.canvas → theme.colors.bg.canvas global.fontSize.display → theme.typography.fontSize.display ``` At this layer, the UI code is not inventing style or message. It is consuming the same upstream truth. ## 5. One-line law for each layer ```text Copy truth = what is said Slide truth = where and why it is said Figma truth = how it is visually composed Frontend truth = how the same system is executed in code ``` ## 6. Correct dependency order ```text copy truth → slide truth → Figma truth → frontend truth ``` Not: ```text design first → copy later ``` And not: ```text frontend improvises from screenshots ``` Because your broader system already requires that downstream layers execute upstream invariants rather than inventing them locally. That is the same logic used across the repo architecture, proof bridge, and operator contracts. fileciteturn3file21 fileciteturn3file24 fileciteturn3file25 ## 7. Canonical transformation map ```text CopyTruth → exact_copy_deck → sales/client/investor variants SlideTruth → slide master content matrix → slide IDs → template bindings FigmaTruth → plugin data schema → token bindings → component + template registries → export registry FrontendTruth → theme map → semantic component map → token sync outputs → runtime surfaces ``` ## 8. Final doctrine ```text Copy is source of meaning. Slides are source of narrative order. Figma is source of rendered design state. Frontend is source of executable interface state. ``` That is the stable chain. The next logical artifact is: ```bash $NEXT="CANONICAL_TRUTH_REGISTRY_V1" ``` where all four layers are defined in one versioned schema.

## User

$NEXT="CANONICAL_TRUTH_REGISTRY_V1"

## Assistant

```bash $NEXT="CANONICAL_TRUTH_REGISTRY_V1" $SYSTEM_NAME="cronus-metabolus" $PRODUCT_SURFACE="auto-content-cannibal" $TRUTH_MODEL="copy_truth → slide_truth → figma_truth → frontend_truth" $REGISTRY_VERSION="v1" ``` Below is the **canonical truth registry** that unifies all four layers into one versioned, machine-readable doctrine. It is the correct next artifact because the system now already has exact copy, slide master logic, Figma plugin/schema logic, and frontend theme mapping; what is missing is the **single source-of-truth registry** that binds them together. fileciteturn3file38 fileciteturn3file37 fileciteturn3file24 # I. PURPOSE ```text CanonicalTruthRegistry = the master semantic contract from which copy, slides, Figma, and frontend all derive. ``` This means: ```text copy truth = source of meaning slide truth = source of narrative structure Figma truth = source of rendered design structure frontend truth = source of executable interface structure ``` Nothing downstream should invent meaning that does not already exist upstream. That matches the broader system law that downstream execution layers must enforce upstream invariants rather than reinterpret them ad hoc. fileciteturn3file21 fileciteturn3file25 --- # II. ROOT SCHEMA ```json { "$schema_id": "cronus_metabolus.canonical_truth_registry.v1", "system_name": "cronus-metabolus", "product_surface": "auto-content-cannibal", "registry_version": "v1", "message_truth": {}, "slide_truth": {}, "figma_truth": {}, "frontend_truth": {}, "transformation_rules": {}, "version_registry": {}, "sync_registry": {} } ``` --- # IV.
